+0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;category&quot;;a:2:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:9:&quot;Community&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}i:1;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:11:&quot;Development&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:33:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/?p=2573&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:1:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:1:{s:11:&quot;isPermaLink&quot;;s:5:&quot;false&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:354:&quot;As [...]&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:8:&quot;Jen Mylo&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:40:&quot;http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/content/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;encoded&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:5071:&quot;&lt;p&gt;As an open source, free software project, WordPress depends on the contributions of hundreds of people from around the globe &amp;#8212; contributions in areas like core code, documentation, answering questions in the support forums, translation, and all the other things it takes to make WordPress the best publishing platform it can be, with the most supportive community. This year, we&amp;#8217;re happy to be participating as a mentoring organization with two respected summer internship programs: &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.google-melange.com/gsoc/homepage/google/gsoc2013&quot;&gt;Google Summer of Code (GSoC)&lt;/a&gt; and the Gnome Outreach Program for Women.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Google Summer of Code&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;GSoC is a summer internship program funded by Google specifically for college/university student developers to work on open source coding projects. We have participated in the Google Summer of Code program in the past, and have enjoyed the opportunity to work with students in this way. Some of our best core developers were GSoC students once upon a time!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/GSoC2013#Mentors&quot;&gt;Our mentors&lt;/a&gt;, almost 30 talented developers with experience developing WordPress, will provide students with guidance and feedback over the course of the summer, culminating in the release of finished projects at the end of the program if all goes well.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Students who successfully complete the program earn $5,000 for their summer efforts. Interested, or know a college student (newly accepted to college counts, too) who should be? All the information you need about our participation in the program, projects, mentors, and the application process is available on the &lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/GSoC2013&quot;&gt;GSoC 2013 page in the Codex&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Gnome Outreach Program for Women&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;It&amp;#8217;s not news that women form a low percentage of contributors in most open source projects, and WordPress is no different. We have great women in the contributor community, including some in fairly visible roles, but we still have a lot of work to do to get a representative gender balance on par with our user base.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The Gnome Outreach Program for Women aims to provide opportunities for women to participate in open source projects, and offers a similar stipend, but there are three key differences between GSoC and Gnome aside from the gender requirement for Gnome.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ol&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size: 13px;line-height: 19px&quot;&gt;The Gnome program allows intern projects in many areas of contribution, not just code. In other words, interns can propose projects like documentation, community management, design, translation, or pretty much any area in which we have people contributing (including code).&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size: 13px;line-height: 19px&quot;&gt;The Gnome Outreach Program for Women doesn&amp;#8217;t require interns to be college students, though students are definitely welcome to participate. This means that women in all stages of life and career can take the opportunity to try working with open source communities for the summer.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size: 13px;line-height: 19px&quot;&gt;We have to help raise the money to pay the interns. Google funds GSoC on its own, and we only have to provide our mentors&amp;#8217; time. Gnome doesn&amp;#8217;t have the same funding, so we need to pitch in to raise the money to cover our interns. If your company is interested in helping with this, please check out the program&amp;#8217;s &lt;/span&gt;&lt;a style=&quot;font-size: 13px;line-height: 19px&quot; href=&quot;https://live.gnome.org/OutreachProgramForWomen#For_Organizations_and_Companies&quot;&gt;sponsorship information&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;font-size: 13px;line-height: 19px&quot;&gt; and follow the contact instructions to get involved. You can earmark donations to support WordPress interns, or to support the program in general. (Pick us, pick us! &lt;img src='http://wordpress.org/news/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_smile.gif' alt=':)' class='wp-smiley' /&gt;  )&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ol&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The summer installment of the Gnome Outreach Program for Women follows the same schedule and general application format as GSoC, though there are more potential projects since it covers more areas of contribution. Women college students interested in doing a coding project are encouraged to apply for both programs to increase the odds of acceptance. All the information you need about our participation in the program, projects, mentors, and the application process is available on the &lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/Gnome_Summer_Program_for_Women&quot;&gt;Gnome Outreach Program for Women page in the Codex&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The application period just started, and it lasts another week (May 1 for Gnome, May 3 for GSoC), so if you think you qualify and are interested in getting involved, check out the information pages, get in touch, and apply… Good luck!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/GSoC2013&quot;&gt;Google Summer of Code 2013 Information&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/Gnome_Summer_Program_for_Women&quot;&gt;Gnome Summer Outreach Program for Women 2013 Information&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

They&amp;#8217;ll be on sale at this price until the anniversary on May 27, and they&amp;#8217;ll start shipping out the week of April 29.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Some people who are planning parties or who organize meetups are already talking about doing group orders to save on shipping costs, which is a great idea &amp;#8212; just make sure you allow enough shipping time. If you&amp;#8217;re not sure if the tees could make it to you in time on your side of the world, use the contact options at the bottom of the store page to ask about shipping times. If they can&amp;#8217;t reach you in time and you want to have a local printer do some for your group, we&amp;#8217;ll post the vector file on the wp10 site within the next week (and this post will get updated accordingly). &lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The shirts are available in black or silvery gray. Why silvery gray? Because of trivia: the traditional gift for 10th anniversaries is tin or aluminum. &lt;img src='http://wordpress.org/news/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_smile.gif' alt=':)' class='wp-smiley' /&gt; &lt;/p&gt;

+0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;category&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Uncategorized&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:33:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/?p=2555&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:1:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:1:{s:11:&quot;isPermaLink&quot;;s:5:&quot;false&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:325:&quot;What&amp;#8217;s We&amp;#8217;re using Meetup Everywhere to coordinate, and will be putting up a website [...]&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:8:&quot;Jen Mylo&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:40:&quot;http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/content/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;encoded&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:2102:&quot;&lt;p&gt;What&amp;#8217;s on May 27, you ask?&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;May 27, 2013 is the &lt;strong&gt;10th anniversary&lt;/strong&gt; of the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2003/05/wordpress-now-available/&quot;&gt;first WordPress release&lt;/a&gt;!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We think this is worth celebrating, and we want WordPress fans all over the world to celebrate with us by throwing their own parties. &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.meetup.com/WordPress/&quot;&gt;We&amp;#8217;re using Meetup Everywhere&lt;/a&gt; to coordinate, and will be putting up a website just for the 10th Anniversary so that we can collect photos, videos, tweets, and posts from all the parties.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The rules are very simple:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ol&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;line-height: 12.997159004211426px&quot;&gt;Pick a place to go where a bunch of people can be merry &amp;#8212; a park, a bar, a backyard, whatever&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Spread the word to local meetups, tech groups, press, etc and get people to say they&amp;#8217;ll come to your party&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;If 50 or more people RSVP to your party, we&amp;#8217;ll try to send you some WordPress stickers and buttons&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Have party attendees post photos, videos, and the like with the #wp10 hashtag&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ol&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We&amp;#8217;ll be using Meetup Everywhere to coordinate parties all over the world, so get your city on the map and &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.meetup.com/WordPress/&quot;&gt;register your party now&lt;/a&gt; !&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We&amp;#8217;ll follow up with registered organizers  over the next few weeks with some tips for how to publicize your party and to get addresses for swag packages. To that end, make sure you check the option that lets WordPress 10th Anniversary know your email, or we won&amp;#8217;t be able to get in touch with you for these things or to give you access to the WP10 blog.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Whose party will be the biggest? The most fun? The most inventive? Will it be yours?&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Note: If you already run a group on meetup.com, making your party an event in your group is great, but you still need to post it and have people RSVP at the &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.meetup.com/WordPress/&quot;&gt;special party page&lt;/a&gt;, because regular groups and Meetup Everywhere groups aren&amp;#8217;t connected yet. &lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

		&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:5:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:7:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:20:&quot;WordPress 3.6 Beta 1&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:55:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2013/04/wordpress-3-6-beta-1/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;comments&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:64:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2013/04/wordpress-3-6-beta-1/#comments&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 04 Apr 2013 17:25:29 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;category&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Uncategorized&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:33:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/?p=2547&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:1:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:1:{s:11:&quot;isPermaLink&quot;;s:5:&quot;false&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:377:&quot;WordPress 3.6 Beta 1 is now available! This is software still in development and we really don’t recommend that you run it on a production site — set up a test site just to play with the new version. To test WordPress 3.6, try the WordPress Beta Tester plugin (you’ll want “bleeding edge nightlies”). Or you can download the beta here (zip). We&amp;#8217;ve [...]&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:12:&quot;Mark Jaquith&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:40:&quot;http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/content/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;encoded&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4085:&quot;&lt;p&gt;WordPress 3.6 Beta 1 is now available!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;This is software still in development and &lt;strong&gt;we &lt;em&gt;really&lt;/em&gt; don’t recommend that you run it on a production site&lt;/strong&gt; — set up a test site just to play with the new version. To test WordPress 3.6, try the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/wordpress-beta-tester/&quot;&gt;WordPress Beta Tester&lt;/a&gt; plugin (you’ll want “bleeding edge nightlies”). Or you can &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/wordpress-3.6-beta1.zip&quot;&gt;download the beta here&lt;/a&gt; (zip).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We&amp;#8217;ve been working for nearly three months and have completed all the features that are slated for this release. This is a bit of a change from the betas of previous release cycles. I felt very strongly that we shouldn&amp;#8217;t release a beta if we were still working on completing the main features. This beta is &lt;strong&gt;actually a beta&lt;/strong&gt;, not an alpha that we&amp;#8217;re calling a beta. If you are a WordPress plugin or theme developer, or a WordPress hosting provider, you should absolutely start testing your code against this new version &lt;strong&gt;now&lt;/strong&gt;. More bugs will be fixed, and some of the features will get polished, but we&amp;#8217;re not going to shove in some big new feature. We&amp;#8217;re ready for you to test it, so jump in there! The more you test the beta, the more stable our release candidates and our final release will be.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;As always, if you think you’ve found a bug, you can post to the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/support/forum/alphabeta&quot;&gt;Alpha/Beta area&lt;/a&gt; in the support forums. Or, if you’re comfortable writing a reproducible bug report, &lt;a href=&quot;http://core.trac.wordpress.org/&quot;&gt;file one on the WordPress Trac&lt;/a&gt;. There, you can also find &lt;a href=&quot;http://core.trac.wordpress.org/report/5&quot;&gt;a list of known bugs&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;http://core.trac.wordpress.org/query?status=closed&amp;amp;group=component&amp;amp;milestone=3.6&quot;&gt;everything we&amp;#8217;ve fixed&lt;/a&gt; so far.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Here&amp;#8217;s what&amp;#8217;s new in 3.6:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Post Formats: &lt;/strong&gt; Post Formats now have their own UI, and theme authors have access to templating functions to access the structured data.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Twenty Thirteen:&lt;/strong&gt; We&amp;#8217;re shipping this year&amp;#8217;s default theme in our first release of the year. Twenty Thirteen is an opinionated, color-rich, blog-centric theme that makes full use of the new Post Formats support.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Audio/Video:&lt;/strong&gt; You can embed audio and video files into your posts without relying on a plugin or a third party media hosting service.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Autosave: &lt;/strong&gt; Posts are now autosaved locally. If your browser crashes, your computer dies, or the server goes offline as you&amp;#8217;re saving, you won&amp;#8217;t lose the your post.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Post Locking: &lt;/strong&gt; See when someone is currently editing a post, and kick them out of it if they fall asleep at the keyboard.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Nav Menus: &lt;/strong&gt; Nav menus have been simplified with an accordion-based UI, and a separate tab for  bulk-assigning menus to locations.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Revisions:&lt;/strong&gt; The all-new revisions UI features avatars, a slider that &amp;#8220;scrubs&amp;#8221; through history, and two-slider range comparisons.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Developers: &lt;/strong&gt; You make WordPress awesome(er). One of the things we strive to do with every release is be compatible with existing plugins and themes. But we need your help. &lt;strong&gt;Please test your plugins and themes against 3.6.&lt;/strong&gt; If something isn&amp;#8217;t quite right, please let us know. (Chances are, it wasn&amp;#8217;t intentional.) If you&amp;#8217;re a forward-thinking theme developer, you should be looking at implementing the new Post Format support in some of your themes (look to Twenty Thirteen for inspiration).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We&amp;#8217;re looking forward to your feedback. If you break it (i.e. find a bug), please report it, and if you’re a developer, try to help us fix it. We&amp;#8217;ve already had more than 150 contributors to version 3.6 — it&amp;#8217;s not too late to join the party!&lt;/p&gt;

3.5.1 Maintenance and Security Release&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:50:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2013/01/wordpress-3-5-1/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;comments&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:59:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2013/01/wordpress-3-5-1/#comments&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 24 Jan 2013 22:23:03 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;category&quot;;a:2:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:8:&quot;Releases&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}i:1;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:8:&quot;Security&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:33:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/?p=2531&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:1:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:1:{s:11:&quot;isPermaLink&quot;;s:5:&quot;false&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:359:&quot;WordPress 3.5.1 is now available. Version 3.5.1 is the first maintenance release of 3.5, fixing 37 bugs. It is also a security release for all previous WordPress versions. For a full list of changes, consult the list of tickets and the changelog, which include: Editor: Prevent certain HTML elements from being unexpectedly removed or modified in rare [...]&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:12:&quot;Andrew Nacin&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:40:&quot;http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/content/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;encoded&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:2499:&quot;&lt;p&gt;WordPress 3.5.1 is now available. Version 3.5.1 is the first maintenance release of 3.5, &lt;a href=&quot;http://core.trac.wordpress.org/milestone/3.5.1&quot;&gt;fixing 37 bugs&lt;/a&gt;. It is also a security release for all previous WordPress versions. For a full list of changes, consult the &lt;a href=&quot;http://core.trac.wordpress.org/query?milestone=3.5.1&quot;&gt;list of tickets&lt;/a&gt; and the &lt;a href=&quot;http://core.trac.wordpress.org/log/branches/3.5?rev=23341&amp;amp;stop_rev=23167&quot;&gt;changelog&lt;/a&gt;, which include:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Editor: Prevent certain HTML elements from being unexpectedly removed or modified in rare cases.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Media: Fix a collection of minor workflow and compatibility issues in the new media manager.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Networks: Suggest proper rewrite rules when creating a new network.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Prevent scheduled posts from being stripped of certain HTML, such as video embeds, when they are published.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Work around some misconfigurations that may have caused some JavaScript in the WordPress admin area to fail.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Suppress some warnings that could occur when a plugin misused the database or user APIs.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Additionally, a bug affecting Windows servers running IIS can prevent updating from 3.5 to 3.5.1. If you receive the error &amp;#8220;Destination directory for file streaming does not exist or is not writable,&amp;#8221; you will need to &lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/Version_3.5.1&quot;&gt;follow the steps outlined on the Codex&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress 3.5.1 also addresses the following security issues:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;A server-side request forgery vulnerability and remote port scanning using pingbacks. This vulnerability, which could potentially be used to expose information and compromise a site, affects all previous WordPress versions. This was fixed by the WordPress security team. We&amp;#8217;d like to thank security researchers &lt;a href=&quot;http://codeseekah.com/&quot;&gt;Gennady Kovshenin&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.ethicalhack3r.co.uk/&quot;&gt;Ryan Dewhurst&lt;/a&gt; for reviewing our work.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Two instances of cross-site scripting via shortcodes and post content. These issues were discovered by Jon Cave of the WordPress security team.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;A cross-site scripting vulnerability in the external library Plupload. Thanks to the Moxiecode team for working with us on this, and for releasing Plupload 1.5.5 to address this issue.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/download/&quot;&gt;Download 3.5.1&lt;/a&gt; or visit Dashboard → Updates in your site admin to update now.&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

		&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:5:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:7:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:17:&quot;2012: A Look Back&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:51:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2013/01/2012-a-look-back/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;comments&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:60:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2013/01/2012-a-look-back/#comments&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Tue, 01 Jan 2013 02:22:20 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;category&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;Uncategorized&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:33:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/?p=2525&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:1:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:1:{s:11:&quot;isPermaLink&quot;;s:5:&quot;false&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:340:&quot;Another year is coming to a close, and it&amp;#8217;s time to look back and reflect on what we&amp;#8217;ve accomplished in the past twelve months. The WordPress community is stronger than ever, and some of the accomplishments of the past year are definitely worth remembering. Software Releases We had two major releases of the WordPress web [...]&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:8:&quot;Jen Mylo&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:40:&quot;http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/content/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;encoded&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4441:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Another year is coming to a close, and it&amp;#8217;s time to look back and reflect on what we&amp;#8217;ve accomplished in the past twelve months. The WordPress community is stronger than ever, and some of the accomplishments of the past year are definitely worth remembering.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;Software Releases&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We had two major releases of the WordPress web application with versions &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2012/06/green/&quot;&gt;3.4&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2012/12/elvin/&quot;&gt;3.5&lt;/a&gt;, as well as 5 security releases during 2012. 3.4 included the theme customizer, while 3.5 became the long awaited &amp;#8220;media release&amp;#8221; featuring a new uploader and gallery management tool. 3.5 contained code contributions from more people than ever, and we hope to continue growing the contributor ranks in the year ahead. We currently have native apps on 6 mobile platforms &amp;#8212; &lt;a href=&quot;http://ios.wordpress.org/&quot;&gt;iOS&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://android.wordpress.org/&quot;&gt;Android&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://blackberry.wordpress.org/&quot;&gt;Blackberry&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://wpwindowsphone.wordpress.com/&quot;&gt;Windows Phone&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://nokia.wordpress.org/&quot;&gt;Nokia&lt;/a&gt;, and &lt;a href=&quot;http://webos.wordpress.org/&quot;&gt;WebOS&lt;/a&gt; &amp;#8212; and saw several updates there as well.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;Plugin Directory&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;A number of improvements were made to the Plugin Directory in 2012. More cosmetic  updates, like the introduction of branded plugin page headers, make it a nicer browsing experience, while functional changes like better-integrated support forums, plugin reviews, and a favorites system made the plugin directory even more useful as a resource.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;The &amp;#8220;Make&amp;#8221; Network and Team Reps&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;2012 was the year that saw the creation of &lt;a href=&quot;http://make.wordpress.org/&quot;&gt;Make.wordpress.org&lt;/a&gt;, a network of sites for the teams of contributors responsible for the different areas of the WordPress project. Now anyone can follow along and get involved with the teams that work on &lt;a href=&quot;http://make.wordpress.org/core/&quot;&gt;core&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://make.wordpress.org/themes/&quot;&gt;theme review&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://make.wordpress.org/support/&quot;&gt;forum support&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://make.wordpress.org/docs/&quot;&gt;documentation&lt;/a&gt;, and more. In 2013 we&amp;#8217;ll work to improve these sites to make it easier to become a contributor. Each team also now has elected Team Reps, a new role that has already led to more cross-team communication. Team reps post each week to the &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/updates/&quot;&gt;Updates blog&lt;/a&gt; so that the other reps can keep up with what&amp;#8217;s going on in other teams.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;WordPress Community Summit&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;At the end of October, about 100 of the most influential and respected members of the WordPress community attended an inaugural &lt;a href=&quot;https://make.wordpress.org/summit&quot;&gt;summit&lt;/a&gt; to discuss where we all stand, and to figure out where we go next with WordPress. A &amp;#8220;conference of conversations,&amp;#8221; this unconference made everyone an active participant, and while not every issue brought to the table was solved by the end of the event, the right questions were being asked.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;Meetup.com&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The WordPress Foundation now has a central account with Meetup.com. We&amp;#8217;ve brought in a couple dozen existing meetup groups as a pilot to test the system, and are in the process of working with more existing meetups (as well as new ones) to join us so that local organizers won&amp;#8217;t have to pay organizer dues and can get more support from the WordPress project.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;Internet Blackout Day&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We participated in the protest against SOPA/PIPA, Internet Blackout Day, on January 18. Though we usually stay out of politics, this campaign was important, and we not only participated in the blackout on WordPress.org, we encouraged our users to do so as well, and recommended plugins to provide blackout functionality. It was deemed the &lt;a href=&quot;http://sopastrike.com/numbers/&quot;&gt;largest online protest in history&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;WordCamps&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;And finally, it wouldn&amp;#8217;t be a recap without counting up the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordcamp.org&quot;&gt;WordCamps&lt;/a&gt;! There were 67 WordCamps around the world in 2012, bringing together WordPress users, developers, and fans. If you didn&amp;#8217;t make it to a WordCamp this year, maybe it can be one of your new year resolutions: &lt;a href=&quot;http://central.wordcamp.org/schedule/&quot;&gt;check the schedule&lt;/a&gt; to find one near you!&lt;/p&gt;

11 Dec 2012 16:54:23 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;category&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:8:&quot;Releases&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:33:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/?p=2517&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:1:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:1:{s:11:&quot;isPermaLink&quot;;s:5:&quot;false&quot;;}}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:363:&quot;It&amp;#8217;s the most wonderful time of the year: a new WordPress release is available and chock-full of goodies to delight bloggers and developers alike. We&amp;#8217;re calling this one &amp;#8220;Elvin&amp;#8221; in honor of drummer Elvin Jones, who played with John Coltrane in addition to many others. If you&amp;#8217;ve been around WordPress a while, the most dramatic [...]&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:14:&quot;Matt Mullenweg&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:40:&quot;http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/content/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;encoded&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:20083:&quot;&lt;p&gt;It&amp;#8217;s the most wonderful time of the year: a new WordPress release &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/download/&quot;&gt;is available&lt;/a&gt; and chock-full of goodies to delight bloggers and developers alike. We&amp;#8217;re calling this one &amp;#8220;Elvin&amp;#8221; in honor of &lt;a href=&quot;http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elvin_Jones&quot;&gt;drummer Elvin Jones&lt;/a&gt;, who played with John Coltrane in addition to many others.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you&amp;#8217;ve been around WordPress a while, the most dramatic new change you&amp;#8217;ll notice is a completely re-imagined flow for uploading photos and creating galleries. Media has long been a friction point and we&amp;#8217;ve listened hard and given a lot of thought into crafting this new system. 3.5 includes a new default theme, Twenty Twelve, which has a very clean mobile-first responsive design and works fantastic as a base for a CMS site. Finally we&amp;#8217;ve spent a lot of time refreshing the styles of the dashboard, updating everything to be Retina-ready with beautiful high resolution graphics, a new color picker, and streamlining a couple of fewer-used sections of the admin.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Here&amp;#8217;s a quick video overview of everything you can share with your friends:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;v-jQDfEbzZ-1&quot; class=&quot;video-player&quot;&gt;&lt;embed id=&quot;v-jQDfEbzZ-1-video&quot; src=&quot;http://s0.videopress.com/player.swf?v=1.03&amp;amp;guid=jQDfEbzZ&amp;amp;isDynamicSeeking=true&quot; type=&quot;application/x-shockwave-flash&quot; width=&quot;692&quot; height=&quot;388&quot; title=&quot;Introducing WordPress 3.5&quot; wmode=&quot;direct&quot; seamlesstabbing=&quot;true&quot; allowfullscreen=&quot;true&quot; allowscriptaccess=&quot;always&quot; overstretch=&quot;true&quot;&gt;&lt;/embed&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;For Developers&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;You can now put your (or anyone&amp;#8217;s) WordPress.org username on the plugins page and see your favorite tagged ones, to make it easy to install them again when setting up a new site. There&amp;#8217;s a new Tumblr importer. New installs no longer show the links manager. Finally for multisite developers &lt;code&gt;switch_to_blog()&lt;/code&gt; is way faster and you can now install MS in a sub-directory. The &lt;a href=&quot;http://underscorejs.org/&quot;&gt;Underscore&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;http://backbonejs.org/&quot;&gt;Backbone&lt;/a&gt; JavaScript libraries are now available. &lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/Version_3.5&quot;&gt;The Codex has a pretty good summary of the developer features above and beyond this&lt;/a&gt;, and you can always &lt;a href=&quot;http://core.trac.wordpress.org/milestone/3.5&quot;&gt;grab a warm beverage and explore Trac directly&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

Show more information about [...]&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:12:&quot;Andrew Nacin&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:40:&quot;http://purl.org/rss/1.0/modules/content/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;encoded&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:1950:&quot;&lt;p&gt;The third release candidate for WordPress 3.5 is now available. We&amp;#8217;ve made a number of changes over the last week since &lt;a title=&quot;WordPress 3.5 Release Candidate 2&quot; href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2012/11/wordpress-3-5-release-candidate-2/&quot;&gt;RC2&lt;/a&gt; that we can&amp;#8217;t wait to get into your hands. Hope you&amp;#8217;re ready to do some testing!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;span style=&quot;line-height: 13px&quot;&gt;Final UI improvements for the new media manager, based on lots of great feedback.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Show more information about uploading errors when they occur.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;When inserting an image into a post, don&amp;#8217;t forget the alternative text.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Fixes for the new admin button styles.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Improvements for mobile devices, Internet Explorer, and right-to-left languages.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Fix cookies for subdomain installs when multisite is installed in a subdirectory.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Fix ms-files.php rewriting for very old multisite installs.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;At this point, we only have a &lt;a href=&quot;http://core.trac.wordpress.org/report/5&quot;&gt;few minor issues&lt;/a&gt; left. If all goes well, you will see WordPress 3.5 very soon. If you run into any issues, please post to the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/support/forum/alphabeta/&quot;&gt;Alpha/Beta area in the support forums&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you&amp;#8217;d like to know what to test, visit the About page (&lt;strong&gt;&lt;img style=&quot;vertical-align: middle&quot; alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;http://wordpress.org/wp-content/themes/twentyten/images/wordpress.png&quot; /&gt; → About&lt;/strong&gt; in the toolbar) and check out the list of features. This is still development software, so your boss may get mad if you install this on a live site. To test WordPress 3.5, try the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/wordpress-beta-tester/&quot;&gt;WordPress Beta Tester&lt;/a&gt; plugin (you&amp;#8217;ll want &amp;#8220;bleeding edge nightlies&amp;#8221;). Or you can &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/wordpress-3.5-RC3.zip&quot;&gt;download the release candidate here (zip)&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;We&amp;#8217;re still working on about a dozen remaining issues, but we hope to deliver WordPress 3.5 to your hands as early as next week. If you&amp;#8217;d like to know what to test, visit the About page (&lt;strong&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;http://wordpress.org/wp-content/themes/twentyten/images/wordpress.png&quot; /&gt; → About&lt;/strong&gt; in the toolbar) and check out the list of features! As usual, this is still development software and we suggest you do not install this on a live site unless you are adventurous.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Think you&amp;#8217;ve found a bug?&lt;/strong&gt; Please post to the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/support/forum/alphabeta/&quot;&gt;Alpha/Beta area in the support forums&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Developers,&lt;/strong&gt; please continue to test your plugins and themes, so that if there is a compatibility issue, we can figure it out before the final release. You can find our &lt;a href=&quot;http://core.trac.wordpress.org/report/6&quot;&gt;list of known issues here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;To test WordPress 3.5, try the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/wordpress-beta-tester/&quot;&gt;WordPress Beta Tester&lt;/a&gt; plugin (you&amp;#8217;ll want &amp;#8220;bleeding edge nightlies&amp;#8221;). Or you can &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/wordpress-3.5-RC2.zip&quot;&gt;download the release candidate here (zip)&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;We hope to ship WordPress 3.5 in &lt;em&gt;two weeks&lt;/em&gt;. But to do that, we need your help! If you haven&amp;#8217;t tested 3.5 yet, there&amp;#8217;s no time like the present. (The oft-repeated warning: Please, not on a live site, unless you&amp;#8217;re adventurous.)&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Think you&amp;#8217;ve found a bug?&lt;/strong&gt; Please post to the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/support/forum/alphabeta/&quot;&gt;Alpha/Beta area in the support forums&lt;/a&gt;. If any known issues come up, you’ll be able to &lt;a href=&quot;http://core.trac.wordpress.org/report/6&quot;&gt;find them here&lt;/a&gt;. &lt;strong&gt;Developers,&lt;/strong&gt; please test your plugins and themes, so that if there is a compatibility issue, we can figure it out before the final release.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;To test WordPress 3.5, try the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/wordpress-beta-tester/&quot;&gt;WordPress Beta Tester&lt;/a&gt; plugin (you&amp;#8217;ll want &amp;#8220;bleeding edge nightlies&amp;#8221;). Or you can &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/wordpress-3.5-RC1.zip&quot;&gt;download the release candidate here (zip)&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you&amp;#8217;d like to know what to &lt;del&gt;break&lt;/del&gt; test, visit the About page (&lt;strong&gt;&lt;img style=&quot;vertical-align: text-top&quot; alt=&quot;&quot; src=&quot;http://wordpress.org/wp-content/themes/twentyten/images/wordpress.png&quot; /&gt; → About&lt;/strong&gt; in the toolbar) and check out the list of features! Trust me, you want to try out media.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Release candidate&lt;/em&gt;&lt;br /&gt;

Today, we&amp;#8217;re excited for you to meet another WordPress enthusiast behind the scenes, reviewing and publishing the best video content for WordPress.tv.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Everyone, meet AJ Morris.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;span id=&quot;more-302&quot;&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;AJ Morris&lt;br /&gt;
Owosso, Michigan&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;How did you get involved with WordPress?&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I started blogging in 2006. WordPress was the natural choice back then, as I liked to fool around with servers and websites. As time went on, I started developing themes and plugins. I now work with a theme company and have several large contracts maintaining and developing WordPress-based websites for companies, bloggers, and everyone in between. I love the ease of use and flexibility that WordPress offers not only to developers, but content creators as well.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;Why did you decide to become a WordPress.tv moderator?&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I love listening to people speak about WordPress. While I can&amp;#8217;t financially support going to every &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptvblog.wordpress.com/feed/central.wordcamp.org&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;WordCamp&lt;/a&gt; every year, I thought the next best thing was to &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/get-involved/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;get involved&lt;/a&gt; by helping to publish the WordCamp videos &amp;#8212; and get to watch them first. It&amp;#8217;s great, simple and fun, and easy to give back just a little to the WordPress community.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;Got any essential tips for people interested in creating high-quality content for WordPress.tv?&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Capture great audio! As nice as it is to see yourself in a video, I actually prefer that if you can&amp;#8217;t get everything done well, to get at least the audio captured as best as you can.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;An external Lavalier microphone on the speaker definitely helps. I&amp;#8217;d also suggest a microphone to pass around for a Q&amp;amp;A session at the end of a presentation. This is helpful, since a lot of speakers don&amp;#8217;t repeat the question.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;There are some great videos on WordPress.tv! What are your favorites?&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/2013/03/17/chris-lema-success-in-distributed-contexts/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Success in Distributed Contexts&lt;/a&gt; by &lt;strong&gt;Chris Lema&lt;/strong&gt;.&lt;/strong&gt; It&amp;#8217;s great to hear the business side of how to work in a distributed environment.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/2013/03/08/paul-clark-how-wordpress-saves-lives-freedom-hope-and-custom-post-types/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;How WordPress Saves &amp;#8212; Freedom, Hope, and Custom Post Types&lt;/a&gt; by &lt;strong&gt;Paul Clark&lt;/strong&gt;.&lt;/strong&gt; A great video on custom post types and how they are used to create applications other than blogs and simple websites.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/2013/02/01/dre-armeda-how-anyone-can-hack-your-wordpress-site-in-less-than-5-minutes-and-what-you-can-do-2&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;How Anyone Can Hack Your WordPress Site in Less than 5 Minutes and What You Can Do&amp;#8230;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; &lt;strong&gt;by Dre Armeda. &lt;/strong&gt;I&amp;#8217;ve met Dre a few times, and everything he says about WordPress security is always spot on. He&amp;#8217;s got great tips and tricks in his videos and presentations that can help everyone, from the beginner to the most advanced WordPress user.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Thanks for chatting with us, AJ!&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Interested in getting involved? &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/apply-to-be-a-wordpress-tv-moderator/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Apply to be a WordPress.tv moderator.&lt;/a&gt; For more on WordPress.tv video best practices, read our &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptvblog.wordpress.com/submission-guidelines/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;submission guidelines&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:52:&quot;Dev Blog: Summer Mentorship Programs: GSoC and Gnome&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:33:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/?p=2573&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:76:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2013/04/summer-mentorship-programs-gsoc-and-gnome/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4860:&quot;&lt;p&gt;As an open source, free software project, WordPress depends on the contributions of hundreds of people from around the globe &amp;#8212; contributions in areas like core code, documentation, answering questions in the support forums, translation, and all the other things it takes to make WordPress the best publishing platform it can be, with the most supportive community. This year, we&amp;#8217;re happy to be participating as a mentoring organization with two respected summer internship programs: &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.google-melange.com/gsoc/homepage/google/gsoc2013&quot;&gt;Google Summer of Code (GSoC)&lt;/a&gt; and the Gnome Outreach Program for Women.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Google Summer of Code&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;GSoC is a summer internship program funded by Google specifically for college/university student developers to work on open source coding projects. We have participated in the Google Summer of Code program in the past, and have enjoyed the opportunity to work with students in this way. Some of our best core developers were GSoC students once upon a time!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/GSoC2013#Mentors&quot;&gt;Our mentors&lt;/a&gt;, almost 30 talented developers with experience developing WordPress, will provide students with guidance and feedback over the course of the summer, culminating in the release of finished projects at the end of the program if all goes well.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Students who successfully complete the program earn $5,000 for their summer efforts. Interested, or know a college student (newly accepted to college counts, too) who should be? All the information you need about our participation in the program, projects, mentors, and the application process is available on the &lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/GSoC2013&quot;&gt;GSoC 2013 page in the Codex&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Gnome Outreach Program for Women&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;It&amp;#8217;s not news that women form a low percentage of contributors in most open source projects, and WordPress is no different. We have great women in the contributor community, including some in fairly visible roles, but we still have a lot of work to do to get a representative gender balance on par with our user base.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The Gnome Outreach Program for Women aims to provide opportunities for women to participate in open source projects, and offers a similar stipend, but there are three key differences between GSoC and Gnome aside from the gender requirement for Gnome.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ol&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;span&gt;The Gnome program allows intern projects in many areas of contribution, not just code. In other words, interns can propose projects like documentation, community management, design, translation, or pretty much any area in which we have people contributing (including code).&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;span&gt;The Gnome Outreach Program for Women doesn&amp;#8217;t require interns to be college students, though students are definitely welcome to participate. This means that women in all stages of life and career can take the opportunity to try working with open source communities for the summer.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;span&gt;We have to help raise the money to pay the interns. Google funds GSoC on its own, and we only have to provide our mentors&amp;#8217; time. Gnome doesn&amp;#8217;t have the same funding, so we need to pitch in to raise the money to cover our interns. If your company is interested in helping with this, please check out the program&amp;#8217;s &lt;/span&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://live.gnome.org/OutreachProgramForWomen#For_Organizations_and_Companies&quot;&gt;sponsorship information&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span&gt; and follow the contact instructions to get involved. You can earmark donations to support WordPress interns, or to support the program in general. (Pick us, pick us! &lt;img src=&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_smile.gif&quot; alt=&quot;:)&quot; class=&quot;wp-smiley&quot; /&gt;  )&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ol&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The summer installment of the Gnome Outreach Program for Women follows the same schedule and general application format as GSoC, though there are more potential projects since it covers more areas of contribution. Women college students interested in doing a coding project are encouraged to apply for both programs to increase the odds of acceptance. All the information you need about our participation in the program, projects, mentors, and the application process is available on the &lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/Gnome_Summer_Program_for_Women&quot;&gt;Gnome Outreach Program for Women page in the Codex&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The application period just started, and it lasts another week (May 1 for Gnome, May 3 for GSoC), so if you think you qualify and are interested in getting involved, check out the information pages, get in touch, and apply… Good luck!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/GSoC2013&quot;&gt;Google Summer of Code 2013 Information&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/Gnome_Summer_Program_for_Women&quot;&gt;Gnome Summer Outreach Program for Women 2013 Information&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 25 Apr 2013 03:18:41 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:8:&quot;Jen Mylo&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:2;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:29:&quot;Donncha: WP Super Cache 1.3.2&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:29:&quot;http://ocaoimh.ie/?p=89498321&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:50:&quot;http://ocaoimh.ie/2013/04/24/wp-super-cache-1-3-2/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3980:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://ocaoimh.ie/y/58&quot;&gt;WP Super Cache&lt;/a&gt; is a full page caching plugin for WordPress that will speed up your website.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;This is a security release and any users of the plugin should update as soon as possible. This release and the last 2 (1.3 and 1.3.1) address the following issues:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt; A visitor to a website using WP Super Cache can remotely execute code by way of a specially crafted comment left on the blog. The comment may even be moderated and it will still cause a problem. If you allow untrusted user content on your site through other means it should also be filtered in a similar way. See the function &lt;code&gt;no_mfunc_in_comments&lt;/code&gt; for the existing filter. This will be mitigated in the next release by using a security keyword in the mfunc/mclude/dynamic-cached-content tag.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt; An XSS vulnerability was found in the plugins settings page of the plugin. This has been fixed as well.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The dynamic cached content features are now disabled by default as they should really have been a long time ago. This was announced in the Upgrade Notice of the previous release so hopefully site owners will be prepared for it. If you depend on this feature you can enable it again on the Advanced Settings page. I would encourage you to use Javascript instead for any dynamic features or use a short cache expiration time.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Support for the &lt;a href=&quot;http://jetpack.me/support/mobile-theme/&quot;&gt;mobile theme in Jetpack&lt;/a&gt; has been added in this release by way of a helper plugin. If you enable this feature in Jetpack you should visit the Plugins tab of WP Super Cache and enable the Jetpack plugin there. Caching will be changed to PHP mode, and mobile device support enabled but you may have to manually remove the WP Super Cache mod_rewrite rules in the .htaccess at the root of your site. &lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I would like to thank WordPress.org user &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/support/topic/pwn3d?replies=19&quot;&gt;kisscsaby&lt;/a&gt; for finding the mfunc problem in WP Super Cache and W3 Total Cache and &lt;a href=&quot;http://blog.futtta.be/2013/04/18/wp-caching-plugin-vulnerability-debrief/&quot;&gt;Frank Goossens&lt;/a&gt; for his help fixing it.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Edit:&lt;/strong&gt; I should have stated this above. I did not know about the issue with mfunc until 3 weeks after kisscsaby posted it to a public forum. I don&amp;#8217;t read every post on the support forum unfortunately and the user &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/support/topic/pwn3d?replies=19#post-4078203&quot;&gt;did not email me&lt;/a&gt;. I released version 1.3 within a day of hearing about the problem. Unfortunately the XSS vulnerability became known 24 hours after that requiring another release within 36 hours of the previous one. When it became clear that mfunc could be exploited still I released version 1.3.2&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I&amp;#8217;m leaning towards removing the mfunc/mclude/dynamic-cached-content feature completely. It&amp;#8217;s only used by a tiny minority of users (who will be inconvenienced, sorry) but it&amp;#8217;s dangerous code to have in the plugin. &lt;/p&gt;

&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:50:&quot;Alex King: Capsule, The Developer’s Code Journal&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://alexking.org/?p=16534&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:71:&quot;http://alexking.org/blog/2013/04/24/capsule-the-developers-code-journal&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:7127:&quot;&lt;p&gt;I&amp;#8217;m very pleased today to announce the release of &lt;a href=&quot;http://crowdfavorite.com/capsule/&quot;&gt;Capsule&lt;/a&gt;, the developer&amp;#8217;s code journal.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://alexking.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/04/capsule-510x185.jpg&quot; alt=&quot;Capsule&quot; width=&quot;480&quot; height=&quot;174&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-medium-img wp-image-16575&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Capsule replaces the scratch document you have open when you&amp;#8217;re coding. Instead of throwing away those notes, code snippets, API responses, ad-hoc todo lists, and outlines, Capsule creates an archive of your development artifacts.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Capsule is a free, Open Source (GPL) product. We chose to build it as a WordPress-based app. I&amp;#8217;m &lt;a href=&quot;http://wpengine.com/2013/03/alex-king-on-the-maturity-of-wordpress/&quot;&gt;on record&lt;/a&gt; saying that WordPress isn&amp;#8217;t a great general purpose app platform but it&amp;#8217;s ideal for journaling apps; and I&amp;#8217;m very pleased we were able to use it for Capsule.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://alexking.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/04/tags-510x218.jpg&quot; alt=&quot;tags&quot; width=&quot;480&quot; height=&quot;205&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-medium-img wp-image-16573&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;With Capsule you&amp;#8217;re using a web app, not managing a traditional WordPress website. You never need to go into the WordPress admin to manage your content &amp;#8211; the code editor loads right in the front-end and you create and edit posts inline.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;
  Metadata is a love note to the future.
&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;You designate projects and add tags via simple @project and #hashtag syntax directly in the content. No fiddly checkbox selection or choosing from dropdown menus. It&amp;#8217;s the freedom and simplicity of a text file with the future benefits of metadata.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://alexking.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/04/filter-510x218.jpg&quot; alt=&quot;filter&quot; width=&quot;480&quot; height=&quot;205&quot; class=&quot;aligncenter size-medium-img wp-image-16571&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Read on for more about how Capsule works and the hows and whys of various features (and how you can use Capsule Server as a collaboration hub). More of a &amp;#8220;try it for yourself&amp;#8221; person? Jump over to the &lt;a href=&quot;http://demo.crowdfavorite.com/capsule/&quot;&gt;online demo&lt;/a&gt; and try it out. Or you can &lt;a href=&quot;http://crowdfavorite.com/capsule/&quot;&gt;download&lt;/a&gt; it (or &lt;a href=&quot;https://github.com/crowdfavorite/wp-capsule&quot;&gt;grab the code from GitHub&lt;/a&gt;) and set it up for yourself. We created Capsule as a WordPress theme &amp;#8211; simply &lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/Using_Themes&quot;&gt;install it as usual&lt;/a&gt; and you&amp;#8217;re set to go.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;hr /&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The idea for Capsule started about a year ago when my friend and Crowd Favorite alumni &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/gordonbrander&quot;&gt;Gordon&lt;/a&gt; tweeted this out:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote class=&quot;twitter-tweet&quot; width=&quot;480&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;Keeping a dev diary has been really helpful.Start each day with a fresh .txt. Jot down TODOs, notes, decisions, things learned, as I go.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;mdash; Gordon Brander (@gordonbrander) &lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/gordonbrander/status/189397714184835073&quot;&gt;April 9, 2012&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The idea of a code journal resonated with me immediately. I&amp;#8217;ve been blogging for more than ten years here, and the act of journaling &amp;#8211; of writing things down &amp;#8211; definitely helps with introspection and to cement important lessons.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;At &lt;a href=&quot;http://crowdfavorite.com&quot;&gt;Crowd Favorite&lt;/a&gt; we believe in the craftsman approach to web development. We believe in constantly learning and sharing knowledge. The idea of a code journal seemed like an obvious and useful tool.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Gordon talked about using text files, but I wasn&amp;#8217;t sold on that implementation. I wanted a system that had the simplicity of using text files, but I also wanted to be able to add some structured data to make it easier to find my notes again later.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I like thinking about how systems and apps can work and fit together. The more I thought about the idea of a code journal, the more I realized that the information I would be recording about what I was building would be useful information to share with my colleagues. Likewise, what they recorded during their development would be interesting and useful for me and other team members. And it just so happens that my team and I are pretty handy with this little Open Source system that&amp;#8217;s designed for journaling&amp;#8230;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We brainstormed about how we&amp;#8217;d want to use the system and firmed up a feature set. These included:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;must be incredibly low friction (it will be competing with using text files)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;no titles for entries (titles are friction)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;a good code (text) editor (after all, this is a developer code journal)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;ability to designate an entry as being part of a specific project&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;ability to add tags (keywords) to entries&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;ability to keep some entries private, but share appropriate entries with the rest of the team&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;As a daily user of Capsule, I&amp;#8217;m proud to say we&amp;#8217;ve accomplished this goal and I&amp;#8217;m very pleased with the smoothness of the user experience.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;While we are releasing version 1.0 today, we&amp;#8217;ve had a functional version Capsule on our &lt;a href=&quot;https://github.com/crowdfavorite&quot;&gt;GitHub&lt;/a&gt; since early May of last year and I&amp;#8217;ve been using it while we&amp;#8217;ve been building it. As we&amp;#8217;ve been implementing features, we&amp;#8217;ve also tweaked the design and implementation based on our actual usage. It&amp;#8217;s always handy to be your own use case.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h2&gt;Capsule Server: Use Capsule With Your Team&lt;/h2&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We&amp;#8217;re actually releasing two products today, Capsule and &lt;a href=&quot;http://crowdfavorite.com/capsule/#server&quot;&gt;Capsule Server&lt;/a&gt;. Capsule is the code journal that each developer can set up for themselves. Capsule Server is a collaboration hub that can accept Capsule entries and make them available to other team members.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I really like the way Capsule and Capsule Server interact. Developers can connect their Capsule install to as many Capsule Servers as they like. They can choose which entries get shared to which Capsule Servers, and which entries stay private &amp;#8211; all of this with the same no-friction approach that makes it so easy to include useful metadata in Capsule entries.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;When you set up a Capsule Server, you define the projects for that Server. When you connect to a Capsule Server, you can chose how to map your local projects to the Capsule Server&amp;#8217;s projects. Any entries for projects that are mapped to a Capsule Server are replicated to that Capsule Server whenever they are saved.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Imagine that WordPress set up a Capsule Server for core development. Perhaps another for plugin development. I could connect to both of those, plus the Crowd Favorite Capsule Server. I would still be journaling in one place, with one tool, but I&amp;#8217;d be sharing my notes with all the various folks I want to collaborate with.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I think Capsule an excellent solution to a problem many of us don&amp;#8217;t even know we have. I hope that it will become a valuable tool for you and your development team.&lt;/p&gt;

&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:70:&quot;Ping-O-Matic: Beyond Ping-O-Matic: Share &amp;amp; Get Social with Plugins&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:32:&quot;http://blog.pingomatic.com/?p=85&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:46:&quot;http://blog.pingomatic.com/2013/04/23/plugins/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3505:&quot;&lt;p&gt;If you use &lt;a href=&quot;http://pingomatic.com/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Ping-O-Matic&lt;/a&gt;, you&amp;#8217;re interested in sharing your stuff with the rest of the world and driving as much traffic to your site as possible.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;You&amp;#8217;ve pinged search engines, but what else can you do? If you&amp;#8217;re all about sharing and traffic building, here&amp;#8217;s a list of plugins to consider:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/jetpack/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Jetpack by WordPress.com&lt;/a&gt;:&lt;/strong&gt; An uber-plugin to supercharge your WordPress site with powerful features previously only available to WordPress.com users. Highlights for those interested in sharing and traffic-building:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;span&gt;Email subscriptions for your blog&amp;#8217;s posts and your post&amp;#8217;s comments.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Social networking enabled comment system.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Integration with and automatic posting to your favorite social networks including Twitter, Facebook, Tumblr, and LinkedIn.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Your readers can easily share your posts via email or their favorite social networks. (Previously provided by the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/sharedaddy/&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;Sharedaddy&lt;/a&gt; plugin.)&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/wordpress-seo/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;WordPress SEO by Yoast:&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/strong&gt;A plugin that helps you write better content and also takes care of all the technical optimization. The plugin assists with page analysis, meta and link elements, XML Sitemaps, RSS optmization, social integration, and more.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/google-analytics-for-wordpress/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Google Analytics for WordPress:&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/strong&gt;Track your site easily with lots of metadata: views per author and category, automatic tracking of outbound clicks and pageviews, and much more.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/wysija-newsletters/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Wysija Newsletters:&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; Spread the word about your site with newsletters! Here, you can create newsletters, post notifications, and autoresponders; as well as manage your subscribers.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/buddypress/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;&lt;strong&gt;BuddyPress: &lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/a&gt;With this plugin, users can create profiles, post messages, connect with others in groups, and  more. You can build a community for a company, school, sports team, or other niche community.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/sociable/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Sociable:&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; A plugin for ratings systems, as well as sharing to numerous sites, including Pinterest, Tumblr, Google+, LinkedIn, and Inbound.org.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/add-link-to-facebook/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Add Link to Facebook:&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/strong&gt;Got a great Facebook following? Take advantage of this by adding links to posts or pages that are published to your Facebook wall.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;To explore more plugins for your site, browse the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;WordPress.org Plugin Directory&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

They&amp;#8217;ll be on sale at this price until the anniversary on May 27, and they&amp;#8217;ll start shipping out the week of April 29.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Some people who are planning parties or who organize meetups are already talking about doing group orders to save on shipping costs, which is a great idea &amp;#8212; just make sure you allow enough shipping time. If you&amp;#8217;re not sure if the tees could make it to you in time on your side of the world, use the contact options at the bottom of the store page to ask about shipping times. If they can&amp;#8217;t reach you in time and you want to have a local printer do some for your group, we&amp;#8217;ll post the vector file on the wp10 site within the next week (and this post will get updated accordingly). &lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The shirts are available in black or silvery gray. Why silvery gray? Because of trivia: the traditional gift for 10th anniversaries is tin or aluminum. &lt;img src=&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_smile.gif&quot; alt=&quot;:)&quot; class=&quot;wp-smiley&quot; /&gt; &lt;/p&gt;

&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:51:&quot;WordPress.tv Blog: Meet the Moderators: Ben Lobaugh&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:36:&quot;http://wptvblog.wordpress.com/?p=297&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:53:&quot;http://wptvblog.wordpress.com/2013/04/22/ben-lobaugh/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3478:&quot;&lt;p&gt;As mentioned in March, we&amp;#8217;ve got a growing team of &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;WordPress.tv&lt;/a&gt; moderators, who review and publish WordCamp and event videos. As we continue on with our Meet the Moderators Q&amp;amp;A series, we&amp;#8217;ll learn more about these volunteers and how they got involved with WordPress, and their tips on submitting video content.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Please say hello to WordPress.tv moderator Ben Lobaugh, from the beautiful shores of Puget Sound.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;span id=&quot;more-297&quot;&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Ben Lobaugh&lt;br /&gt;
Seattle, Washington&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;How did you get involved with WordPress?&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I started using WordPress in the early days because it seemed I was never able to get around to completing the CMS I was writing. WordPress gave me the power and flexibility I needed, and as it grew and matured, I fell more and more in love with it. With version 2.8, I almost exclusively put clients on WordPress, and as of 3.0 I&amp;#8217;ve abandoned all other CMS platforms in favor of the powerhouse WordPress has become.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;Why did you decide to become a WordPress.tv moderator?&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Well, first off the videos of me were not being published as quickly as I wanted! &lt;img src=&quot;http://s1.wp.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_wink.gif&quot; alt=&quot;;)&quot; class=&quot;wp-smiley&quot; /&gt;  The videos on WordPress.tv have been useful to me, and the community has given me so much. Moderating videos on WordPress.tv is a simple and enjoyable way of giving back to this community.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;Got any essential tips for people interested in creating high-quality content for WordPress.tv?&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I highly recommend ensuring the camera will interface into your existing hardware before shooting anything; I ran into a hardware incompatibility issue when trying to pull WordCamp Seattle video from the camera. Another very important tip is to get an external (probably shotgun) microphone to ensure the speaker&amp;#8217;s voice is crisp and clear.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h4&gt;There are some great videos on WordPress.tv! What are your favorites?&lt;/h4&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I get giddy if I see &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/?s=Morten+Rand-Hendriksen&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Morten Rand-Hendriksen&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/?s=tony+perez&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Tony Perez&lt;/a&gt;, or &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/?s=Zack+Tollman&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Zack Tollman&lt;/a&gt; on a &lt;a href=&quot;http://central.wordcamp.org/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;WordCamp&lt;/a&gt; speaker list! These guys are incredibly fun and engaging speakers that can make any technical subject easy to understand. I highly recommend watching their videos. Even if you don&amp;#8217;t know anything about the subject, you&amp;#8217;ll enjoy watching their antics.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Thanks for chatting with us, Ben! &lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Interested in &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/get-involved/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;getting involved&lt;/a&gt;? &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/apply-to-be-a-wordpress-tv-moderator/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;Apply to be a WordPress.tv moderator.&lt;/a&gt; For more on WordPress.tv video best practices, read our &lt;a href=&quot;http://wptvblog.wordpress.com/submission-guidelines/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;submission guidelines&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
