&lt;br /&gt;  &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; href=&quot;http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/gocomments/wptv.wordpress.com/18707/&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/comments/wptv.wordpress.com/18707/&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt; &lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://stats.wordpress.com/b.gif?host=wordpress.tv&amp;blog=5089392&amp;post=18707&amp;subd=wptv&amp;ref=&amp;feed=1&quot; width=&quot;1&quot; height=&quot;1&quot; /&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/2013/04/22/brian-krogsgard-going-for-it-how-to-become-a-respected-wordpress-developer/&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Going For It- How to Become a Respected WordPress Developer.mp4&quot; src=&quot;http://videos.videopress.com/1t0BIt3c/video-894afa8191_std.original.jpg&quot; width=&quot;160&quot; height=&quot;120&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Mon, 22 Apr 2013 17:30:03 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:12:&quot;WordPress.tv&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:13;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:25:&quot;Matt: Jawbone UP vs Basis&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:21:&quot;http://ma.tt/?p=42347&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:41:&quot;http://ma.tt/2013/04/jawbone-up-vs-basis/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:5623:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-thumbnail wp-image-42349 alignright&quot; alt=&quot;Jawbone UP&quot; src=&quot;http://i2.wp.com/s.ma.tt/files/2013/04/jawbone-up.jpg?resize=195%2C139&quot; /&gt; I&amp;#8217;ve always been into personal analytics. From Wakemate to the Nike Fuelband I&amp;#8217;ve tried pretty much every device that&amp;#8217;s come on the market to help you become more self-aware of your activities, and hopefully improve them as well.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Lately I&amp;#8217;ve settled on two that I think are really high quality: the &lt;a href=&quot;https://jawbone.com/up&quot;&gt;Jawbone UP&lt;/a&gt; and the &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.mybasis.com/&quot;&gt;Basis watch&lt;/a&gt;. I would recommend either above the Nike Fuelband or Fitbit, but let me share some brief thoughts about my experiences with each:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The UP is beautiful &amp;#8212; it&amp;#8217;s easy to wear with pretty much any outfit, even with formal wear I find I can move it up my arm a little bit inside my sleeve above my shirt cuff thanks to the flexible nature of the band. The social app they have for it is cool, though it can be a little weird to see your teammate&amp;#8217;s minute-by-minute sleeping habits (&amp;#8220;Hey! I noticed you were up between 3:32 and 3:50 AM last night. How &amp;#8217;bout them Giants?&amp;#8221;).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;attachment_42350&quot; class=&quot;wp-caption alignleft&quot;&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/s.ma.tt/files/2013/04/IMG_6138.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot; wp-image-42350  &quot; alt=&quot;I'm very proud of my sleep.&quot; src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/s.ma.tt/files/2013/04/IMG_6138.png?resize=150%2C266&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;wp-caption-text&quot;&gt;I&amp;#8217;m very proud of my sleep.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The battery life is over a week so you never have to think about it, but you do have to carry around a proprietary connector for it which I keep losing leaving me (like right now) with an uncharged and useless device. To sync you plug the band into your phone&amp;#8217;s headphone port and the sync takes a few seconds, it&amp;#8217;s a fun process I do usually first thing in the morning to see how I slept the night before and it&amp;#8217;s also fun to demo to friends. The first one I had was in their &amp;#8220;mint green&amp;#8221; color and I ended up wearing it out &amp;#8212; it started to look dirty and I broke it where the headphone jack comes out making it difficult to charge and sync. That said, I was pretty rough on it. My new one is blue and I like it much better. My only big complaint about how the whole thing works is it doesn&amp;#8217;t detect when you go to sleep, you have to press and hold the button on the end to put it from wake to sleep mode, which I would frequently forget to do. I really like the idea of the smart alarm and power nap features even though I never used them.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;alignright size-thumbnail wp-image-42348&quot; alt=&quot;Basis B1 Band&quot; src=&quot;http://i1.wp.com/s.ma.tt/files/2013/04/b1-basis-band.jpg?resize=195%2C139&quot; /&gt;The Basis is a bit clunky and retro looking, but functionality-wise it provides &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.mybasis.com/basis-healthy-habits-technology/&quot;&gt;some really cool data&lt;/a&gt;: it tracks your heart rate, skin temperature, perspiration level, steps, and sleep. It detects automatically when you&amp;#8217;re asleep, no buttons to push. The data is presented in a really cool web app that lets you compare some of the data points and that I learned cool things from, like my heart rate jumps about 20 beats per minute when I wake up, and I&amp;#8217;m most warm about two thirds into my sleep cycle. There don&amp;#8217;t appear any social features that I&amp;#8217;ve seen in the software, though its habit formation tracking seems pretty slick. The way the &amp;#8220;buttons&amp;#8221; work on the device is pretty cool, the silver dots in the corners are touch-sensitive. There&amp;#8217;s a button on the side that I haven&amp;#8217;t figured out what it does yet. Syncing and charging is much worse than the UP &amp;#8212; it&amp;#8217;s got an even clunkier proprietary USB thing that both syncs to your computer and charges, but because the display can show you how you&amp;#8217;re doing as you go throughout the day I don&amp;#8217;t feel the need to synchronize it as often. The heart rate tracking is by far my favorite feature. It&amp;#8217;s comfortable to wear, but doesn&amp;#8217;t disappear like the UP. Finally, as an added bonus, it tells the time. (Surprising useful.) If it somehow merged with &lt;a href=&quot;http://getpebble.com/&quot;&gt;the Pebble&lt;/a&gt; I&amp;#8217;d be in geek heaven.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If I had to pick between the two I&amp;#8217;d just use the Basis. The awkwardness of the device is outweighed by the richness of the data it provides. For right now I&amp;#8217;m not choosing: I wear one on each wrist and compare the data. (It&amp;#8217;s always within a few % of each other for things they both do.) If I were hiking in the woods for a week I&amp;#8217;d probably just take the UP as its battery would last the entire time. It&amp;#8217;s really illustrated for me what a silo each of these systems are, they don&amp;#8217;t talk to each other at all and it appears unlikely they ever will.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Long-term I think we really need an open source package you can run on your own servers that can ingest the data from all of these services, say from back when I used to use a &lt;a href=&quot;http://wakemate.com/&quot;&gt;Wakemate&lt;/a&gt; sleep tracking to today&amp;#8217;s &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.fitbit.com/aria&quot;&gt;Fitbit Aria&lt;/a&gt; scale, the meals I track in the UP app with my Basis heart rate data and &lt;a href=&quot;http://runkeeper.com/&quot;&gt;Runkeeper&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.hundredpushups.com/&quot;&gt;Hundred Pushup&lt;/a&gt; logs, and provide you with a single data store for all the personal analytics you generate across various services. I think there&amp;#8217;s going to be a lot of competition in this space in the next few years.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Mon, 22 Apr 2013 17:05:28 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4:&quot;Matt&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:14;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;

&lt;br /&gt;  &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; href=&quot;http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/gocomments/wptv.wordpress.com/18729/&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/comments/wptv.wordpress.com/18729/&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt; &lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://stats.wordpress.com/b.gif?host=wordpress.tv&amp;blog=5089392&amp;post=18729&amp;subd=wptv&amp;ref=&amp;feed=1&quot; width=&quot;1&quot; height=&quot;1&quot; /&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/2013/04/17/erick-arbe-wordpress-navigation-in-responsive-design/&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;WordPress Navigation in Responsive Design.mp4&quot; src=&quot;http://videos.videopress.com/ixOlP9OU/video-40e99c6285_scruberthumbnail_0.jpg&quot; width=&quot;160&quot; height=&quot;120&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 18 Apr 2013 02:33:00 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:12:&quot;WordPress.tv&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:23;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:60:&quot;WP Android: Version 2.3 is Here: New User Interface and More&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:35:&quot;http://android.wordpress.org/?p=759&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:52:&quot;http://android.wordpress.org/2013/04/17/2-3-release/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:6310:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wpandroid.files.wordpress.com/2013/04/wordpress-for-android-version-2-3-devices2.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://wpandroid.files.wordpress.com/2013/04/wordpress-for-android-version-2-3-devices2.jpg?w=620&amp;h=454&quot; alt=&quot;Version 2.3 of WordPress for Android: menu drawer and action bar&quot; width=&quot;620&quot; height=&quot;454&quot; class=&quot;alignnone size-large wp-image-816&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Today, we&amp;#8217;ve jubilantly released version 2.3 of &lt;a href=&quot;http://android.wordpress.org/&quot;&gt;WordPress for Android&lt;/a&gt; to &lt;a href=&quot;https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=org.wordpress.android&amp;hl=en&quot;&gt;Google Play&lt;/a&gt;. After updating, you&amp;#8217;ll see right away that this release includes very exciting updates to the user interface. Let&amp;#8217;s dive in to what&amp;#8217;s new!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Action Bar&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wpandroid.files.wordpress.com/2013/04/wordpress-for-android-version-2-3-action-bar-on-nexus-7.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://wpandroid.files.wordpress.com/2013/04/wordpress-for-android-version-2-3-action-bar-on-nexus-7.jpg?w=620&amp;h=295&quot; alt=&quot;Version 2.3 of WordPress for Android: action bar on a Nexus 7&quot; width=&quot;620&quot; height=&quot;295&quot; class=&quot;alignnone size-large wp-image-819&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
You&amp;#8217;ll notice a fresh, new look. We&amp;#8217;ve taken into account Android&amp;#8217;s &amp;#8220;Holo&amp;#8221; style guidelines and implemented the Action Bar interface throughout the app. If you&amp;#8217;ve used any other apps designed for Android 4.0 or higher, you&amp;#8217;ll feel right at home with the new user interface. Your Action Bar provides easy access to common actions such as creating a new post, refreshing, and sharing to other apps.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We also couldn&amp;#8217;t resist making the Action Bar in WordPress blue. &lt;img src=&quot;http://s1.wp.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_wink.gif&quot; alt=&quot;;)&quot; class=&quot;wp-smiley&quot; /&gt; &lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Menu Drawer&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wpandroid.files.wordpress.com/2013/04/wordpress-for-android-version-2-3-menu-drawer-on-samsung-galaxy-s3-update.jpg&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://wpandroid.files.wordpress.com/2013/04/wordpress-for-android-version-2-3-menu-drawer-on-samsung-galaxy-s3-update.jpg?w=242&amp;h=491&quot; alt=&quot;Version 2.3 of WordPress for Android: menu drawer on Samsung Galaxy S3&quot; width=&quot;242&quot; height=&quot;491&quot; class=&quot;alignright size-medium wp-image-822&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The older-style &lt;a href=&quot;http://android.wordpress.org/2011/12/19/version-2-0-android-blogging-re-imagined/&quot;&gt;dashboard&lt;/a&gt; user interface has been replaced with a Menu Drawer for quick and easy navigation to other areas of the app from wherever you are. You&amp;#8217;ll find all of the same actions the dashboard had, but with the addition of some nifty new ones.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;To access the menu, simply tap the arrow next to the WordPress logo &amp;#8211; in the top-left corner of the app &amp;#8212; or swipe from the left side of the screen. If you&amp;#8217;re on a large tablet device, the menu will always be visible, which takes advantage of the extra screen space. If you have multiple blogs in the app, you&amp;#8217;ll see a drop-down list at the top of your Menu Drawer that you can access to quickly switch to another blog to work with, right in the app.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;When you leave the app, it will remember the last selection you made in the Menu Drawer so when you return, you can pick up where you left off.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Other new features&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In addition to the revamped user interface, you&amp;#8217;ll find these new features as well:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;strong&gt;View Site option&lt;/strong&gt;. A &lt;em&gt;View Site&lt;/em&gt; option has been added to the Menu Drawer so you can view your blogs from within the app.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Admin area access.&lt;/strong&gt; You can access the wp-admin areas of your WordPress.com blogs by loading the &lt;em&gt;Dashboard&lt;/em&gt; option in the Menu Drawer.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Faster loading.&lt;/strong&gt; The WordPress.com Reader now takes advantage of caching for faster loading.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Updated look and feel.&lt;/strong&gt; Settings have been converted to use the Android standard for preferences, giving them the Holo look and feel on supported devices. Many views have been updated to the Holo look and feel as well, including the post editor and all list views.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Improved post editor experience.&lt;/strong&gt; The post editor now has an expandable content area, which makes it much easier to navigate around the post content when you&amp;#8217;re editing.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Improved image uploading.&lt;/strong&gt; If a post has an image but fails to upload the image, the post will be saved as a draft first &amp;#8212; instead of published &amp;#8212; so the image upload can be corrected.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Thanks &amp;#8212; and what&amp;#8217;s next&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We thank the developers who worked so hard on this release &amp;#8211; &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/support/profile/mrroundhill&quot;&gt;mrroundhill&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/support/profile/willnorris&quot;&gt;willnorris&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/support/profile/isaackeyet&quot;&gt;isaackeyet&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/support/profile/daniloercoli&quot;&gt;daniloercoli&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/support/profile/aerych&quot;&gt;aerych&lt;/a&gt; &amp;#8211; as well as the beta testers who tried out the app over at the &lt;a href=&quot;http://dev.android.wordpress.org&quot;&gt;Developer Blog&lt;/a&gt;. Great work, all!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We also thank &lt;a href=&quot;http://jakewharton.com/&quot;&gt;Jake Wharton&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;http://simonvt.net/&quot;&gt;Simon Vig Therkildsen&lt;/a&gt; for creating the ActionBarSherlock and android-menudrawer libraries that enabled us to use the Action Bar and Menu Drawer on older Android devices. Good stuff!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;What&amp;#8217;s next? We&amp;#8217;re looking at adding notifications to the app so you can keep up with what&amp;#8217;s happening on your WordPress sites while mobile and on the go.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;What would you like to see added to the app?&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Want to contribute?&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Don&amp;#8217;t forget that WordPress for Android is an open source project. Want to get involved? Check out &lt;a href=&quot;http://make.wordpress.org/mobile&quot;&gt;make.wordpress.org/mobile&lt;/a&gt; to get started.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Finally, we&amp;#8217;re always excited to get feedback on the app. Please feel free to leave a comment here or send a tweet to &lt;a href=&quot;http://twitter.com/wpandroid&quot;&gt;@WPAndroid&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:26:&quot;Alex King: Scared Straight&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://alexking.org/?p=16510&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:51:&quot;http://alexking.org/blog/2013/04/17/scared-straight&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:1207:&quot;.threads-post-notice {

	padding: 10px;

	font-weight: bold;
}

&lt;p&gt;I woke up to a bit of a scare when some of my alexking.org Gmail accounts were unable to log in to Gmail. I was afraid the accounts had been compromised and the passwords changed. I had secure passwords, but had been lazy about turning on 2-factor authentication for several of them &amp;#8211; that&amp;#8217;s all fixed now.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;As it turned out, the hiccup ended up being due to a Gmail disruption.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I&amp;#8217;ve also turned on 2-factor authentication for this site using &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/google-authenticator/&quot;&gt;this plugin&lt;/a&gt; (make sure to enable the app key if you use iOS or Android apps to connect to your site). Note that the Social logins for commenting still work without 2-factor authentication.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I&amp;#8217;d recommend taking similar steps for your sites. Waking up to an &amp;#8220;uh-oh&amp;#8221; feeling is no fun at all.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;p&gt;Any icon artists out there interested in creating an application icon for a free (GPL) WordPress-based app that @crowdfavorite is working on?&lt;/p&gt;

&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:35:&quot;bbPress: bbPress 2.3 now available!&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://bbpress.org/?p=133122&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:58:&quot;http://bbpress.org/blog/2013/04/bbpress-2-3-now-available/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:40056:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Out now is &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/bbpress/&quot;&gt;bbPress 2.3&lt;/a&gt;!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;It comes with over 150 individual fixes and enhancements since 2.2, and is a safe update to any site running bbPress 2.0 or higher.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Here are some notable changes in 2.3:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;WordPress 3.6 tested&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Forum-wide Search!&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Performance and caching improvements&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Vanilla, Mingle, and SimplePress importers&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Improved to importer bbcode handling&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Improved theme compatibility with new template-stack API&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Improved BuddyPress Group Forum, Activity Streams, and Profiles integration&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Improved Roles and Capabilities&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Improved code documentation&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Improved RTL and fixed missing translations&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Improved sub-action execution order to fix user/login issues&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Added Statistics shortcode&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Major props to the following individuals for helping make 2.3 a success: alexvorn2, alex-ye, anointed, boonebgorges, cnorris23, daveshine, DJPaul, duck_, ericlewis, fartlek, jaredatch, jmdodd, Kaspace, mamaduka, markmcwilliams, mercime, mesayre, michelwppi, mouratidis, MZAWeb, nacin, netweb, Omicron7, pavelevap, ryangannon, scribu, schrepel, sorich87, tungdo, vibol, Viper007Bond, westi, and wonderboymusic. (If you&amp;#8217;re missing, ping me!)&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/bbpress/&quot;&gt;Go download bbPress 2.3!&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;

		&lt;p&gt;For people wanting to hide the new search box, add this to your theme&amp;#8217;s CSS:
&lt;pre&gt;&lt;code&gt;.bbp-search-form {
    display:none !important;
}&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;
&lt;p&gt;For the admin area, after further investigation, the only reason I saw the Forums, Topics and Replies menus at all was because of my Post Calendar plugin. Once I disabled that, the Admin menus for bbPress disappeared entirely.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;And I&amp;#8217;m with &lt;a href=&quot;http://bbpress.org/forums/profile/wildomains/&quot; rel=&quot;nofollow&quot;&gt;@wildomains&lt;/a&gt;, I had to disable &amp;#8216;bbPress moderation&amp;#8217; to get to see the posts. I want to have that plugin, so hopefully either they will update, or whatever change in bbPress broke it can be changed back.&lt;/p&gt;

&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:53:&quot;Alex King: Backward Compatible WP Heartbeat API Usage&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://alexking.org/?p=16470&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:78:&quot;http://alexking.org/blog/2013/04/14/backward-compatible-wp-heartbeat-api-usage&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:448:&quot;&lt;p&gt;I wanted to utilize the &lt;a href=&quot;http://core.trac.wordpress.org/ticket/23216&quot;&gt;WP 3.6 heartbeat API&lt;/a&gt; in an app I&amp;#8217;m working on. I also wanted to include this feature before WordPress 3.6 officially shipped, so that meant it had to be compatible with WordPress 3.5.x as well.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Turns out, it&amp;#8217;s really easy. The heartbeat API looks excellent.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;p&gt;View the code on &lt;a href=&quot;https://gist.github.com/5381074&quot;&gt;Gist&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Sun, 14 Apr 2013 17:52:49 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4:&quot;Alex&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:29;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Matt: Passwords and Brute Force&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:21:&quot;http://ma.tt/?p=42342&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:47:&quot;http://ma.tt/2013/04/passwords-and-brute-force/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:1404:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Almost 3 years ago we released a version of WordPress (&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2010/06/thelonious/&quot;&gt;3.0&lt;/a&gt;) that allowed you to pick a custom username on installation, which largely ended people using &amp;#8220;admin&amp;#8221; as their default username. Right now there&amp;#8217;s a botnet going around all of the WordPresses it can find trying to login with the &amp;#8220;admin&amp;#8221; username and a bunch of common passwords, and it has turned into a news story (especially from companies that sell &amp;#8220;solutions&amp;#8221; to the problem).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Here&amp;#8217;s what I would recommend: If you still use &amp;#8220;admin&amp;#8221; as a username on your blog, &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.digitalkonline.com/blog/change-your-wordpress-admin-username/&quot;&gt;change it&lt;/a&gt;, use a &lt;a href=&quot;http://en.support.wordpress.com/selecting-a-strong-password/&quot;&gt;strong password&lt;/a&gt;, if you&amp;#8217;re on WP.com &lt;a href=&quot;http://en.blog.wordpress.com/2013/04/05/two-step-authentication/&quot;&gt;turn on two-factor authentication&lt;/a&gt;, and of course make sure you&amp;#8217;re up-to-date on the latest version of WordPress. Do this and you&amp;#8217;ll be ahead of 99% of sites out there and probably never have a problem. Most other advice isn&amp;#8217;t great &amp;#8212; supposedly this botnet has over 90,000 IP addresses, so an IP limiting or login throttling plugin isn&amp;#8217;t going to be great (they could try from a different IP a second for 24 hours).&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Fri, 12 Apr 2013 23:55:11 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4:&quot;Matt&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:30;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;

&lt;br /&gt;  &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; href=&quot;http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/gocomments/wptv.wordpress.com/18636/&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/comments/wptv.wordpress.com/18636/&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt; &lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://stats.wordpress.com/b.gif?host=wordpress.tv&amp;blog=5089392&amp;post=18636&amp;subd=wptv&amp;ref=&amp;feed=1&quot; width=&quot;1&quot; height=&quot;1&quot; /&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/2013/04/12/jeremy-pry-an-introduction-to-wordpress-multisite/&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Jeremy Pry: An Introduction to WordPress Multisite&quot; src=&quot;http://videos.videopress.com/gM1IUiuf/jeremy_pry_scruberthumbnail_0.jpg&quot; width=&quot;160&quot; height=&quot;120&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Fri, 12 Apr 2013 12:44:10 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:12:&quot;WordPress.tv&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:34;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:62:&quot;BuddyPress: It’s time to update your BuddyPress installation&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;http://buddypress.org/?p=161349&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:78:&quot;http://buddypress.org/2013/04/its-time-to-update-your-buddypress-installation/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3149:&quot;&lt;p&gt;With the release of BuddyPress 1.7 just a few days ago, and with almost 1.5 million downloads behind us, I wanted to take the time to remind everyone about what&amp;#8217;s gone into improving BuddyPress recently, and to reassure everyone that it&amp;#8217;s okay to update.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In the early days of BuddyPress, things were in flux. Andy and I were furiously building components and features, deprecating code, refactoring the way things worked, and generally tearing up the codebase over and over again. It helped us build a great foundation, but it made updating to the next version a scary and frustrating experience. To those that remember those days, I apologize; to everyone else, I&amp;#8217;m sorry you missed out on the fun. &lt;img src=&quot;http://buddypress.org/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_smile.gif&quot; alt=&quot;:)&quot; class=&quot;wp-smiley&quot; /&gt; &lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Whenever your WordPress installation checks to see if BuddyPress needs an update, the WordPress.org Extend API remembers the current version of BuddyPress that you&amp;#8217;re running. This is how we know (with relative accuracy) approximately how many of what versions are out in the wild, and it&amp;#8217;s also how we generated the pinwheel below, taken from the Stats page from WordPress.org Extend:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;attachment_161350&quot; class=&quot;wp-caption aligncenter&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot; wp-image-161350   &quot; alt=&quot;Active BuddyPress Versions&quot; src=&quot;http://buddypress.org/wp-content/uploads/1/2013/04/Screen-Shot-2013-04-11-at-3.18.43-PM.png&quot; width=&quot;576&quot; height=&quot;283&quot; /&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;wp-caption-text&quot;&gt;Every color of the rainbow is clearly represented&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Despite the pretty colors, this pie chart is actually a little scary. There are so many old and outdated installations of BuddyPress out there, not taking advantage of the neat new features, and not running the most stable and secure code available. The irony is, this is largely our fault.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;These days, BuddyPress is a 1 click update in your WordPress dashboard, and we&amp;#8217;ve built a bunch of API&amp;#8217;s that allow third party plugin developers to write plugins that won&amp;#8217;t break when BuddyPress needs an update. We&amp;#8217;ve spent a large part of the past 2 years reinforcing the foundation we invested in, so that no one needs to be afraid to update BuddyPress ever again.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Starting with BuddyPress 1.8, the core team will be focusing our efforts on including automated tests with each enhancement and critical bug fix, to help ensure that each future release gets more stable than the release before it. Boone Gorges and Paul Gibbs both donated huge amounts of labor building a test suite that is already committed into our development branch, just days after BuddyPress 1.7 was packaged up. Their dedication towards making BuddyPress stable and amazing for everyone is unwavering, and their contributions are truly awesome.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you&amp;#8217;re running an old version of BuddyPress, I urge you to check out and update to BuddyPress 1.7. It&amp;#8217;s the culmination of thousands of hours of effort, and is the most stable, secure, and performant version of BuddyPress yet. Help us change that pinwheel into more of a Pac-Man or a circle.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 11 Apr 2013 21:02:25 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:17:&quot;John James Jacoby&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:35;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:55:&quot;Andrew Nacin: Keynoting php[tek] in Chicago, May 14-17&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:24:&quot;http://nacin.com/?p=4090&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:57:&quot;http://nacin.com/2013/04/11/tek13-php-conference-keynote/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3466:&quot;&lt;p&gt;I&amp;#8217;m excited to announce &lt;strong&gt;I&amp;#8217;m giving a keynote address at &lt;a href=&quot;http://tek.phparch.com/&quot;&gt;php[tek] 2013&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;. It&amp;#8217;s a fantastic PHP conference put on by the folks behind &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.phparch.com/&quot;&gt;php|architect&lt;/a&gt;. &amp;#8220;The premier professional PHP conference with a community flair,&amp;#8221; #tek13 has a rockstar &lt;a href=&quot;http://tek.phparch.com/speakers/&quot;&gt;speaker line-up&lt;/a&gt;, four tracks of content, and a day of training. I&amp;#8217;m thrilled to be attending the conference &amp;#8212; I also attended #tek11 &amp;#8212; let alone speaking.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Last night I tested a few ideas at the &lt;a href=&quot;http://meetup.com/dc-php&quot;&gt;DC PHP meetup&lt;/a&gt; and got some great feedback from the attendees. Some early reviews:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote class=&quot;twitter-tweet&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/wardnetinc/status/322140560523673601&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote class=&quot;twitter-tweet&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/kingkool68/status/322151835756544000&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote class=&quot;twitter-tweet&quot;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;https://twitter.com/openwestconf/status/322393612249886720&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I&amp;#8217;m continuing to conduct a &lt;em&gt;lot&lt;/em&gt; of research for this talk. There&amp;#8217;s a lot WordPress has learned over the years, so I&amp;#8217;ve been searching through the codebase and old commit messages, as well as compiling a ton of data and statistics. If you have anything you think might help, please &lt;a href=&quot;http://gravatar.com/nacin&quot;&gt;contact me&lt;/a&gt;. Here&amp;#8217;s the full talk description:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;
&lt;strong&gt;WordPress is Everywhere: Extreme Portability as a Double-Edged Sword&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress has tens of millions of users worldwide and powers over a fifth of new sites. But such a large and diverse user base presents unique challenges, and as it approaches its tenth birthday, the WordPress codebase is showing its age. So why is it so ubiquitous?&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The answer lies not in its UI, UX, ecosystem, or community, though those are certainly among its strengths. The answer lies instead in a core philosophy that holds the user above all else.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;This user-centric design starts not with the interface, but rather with the code itself. Developers should approach software development with an unwavering promise they will deal with the nonsense instead of passing it off to the user.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Some WordPress positions might seem draconian and inflexible. Backwards compatibility is almost never broken. The technical requirements appeal to lowest common denominators. But because the project maintainers deal with all the pain — technical debt, difficulties with PHP, working on as many server configurations (and misconfigurations) as possible — its users don’t have to. Thanks to the WordPress project’s portability efforts, you can pick a web host or a PHP configuration at random and WordPress will run on it. Because of this, adoption has soared.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The way WordPress operates is not for everyone. But whether your projects are used by 10 users, or 10 million, it may help you to see your code in an entirely new light.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Tickets are &lt;a href=&quot;http://tek.phparch.com/&quot;&gt;still available&lt;/a&gt;. Hope to see you there!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p class=&quot;share-sfc-stc&quot;&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://twitter.com/share?url=http%3A%2F%2Fwp.me%2FpQEdq-13Y&amp;count=horizontal&amp;related=nacin&amp;text=Keynoting%20php%5Btek%5D%20in%20Chicago%2C%20May%2014-17&quot; class=&quot;twitter-share-button&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 11 Apr 2013 17:33:47 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:12:&quot;Andrew Nacin&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:36;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Dev Blog: Save the Date: May 27&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:33:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/?p=2555&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:55:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2013/04/save-the-date-may-27/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:2059:&quot;&lt;p&gt;What&amp;#8217;s on May 27, you ask?&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;May 27, 2013 is the &lt;strong&gt;10th anniversary&lt;/strong&gt; of the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2003/05/wordpress-now-available/&quot;&gt;first WordPress release&lt;/a&gt;!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We think this is worth celebrating, and we want WordPress fans all over the world to celebrate with us by throwing their own parties. &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.meetup.com/WordPress/&quot;&gt;We&amp;#8217;re using Meetup Everywhere&lt;/a&gt; to coordinate, and will be putting up a website just for the 10th Anniversary so that we can collect photos, videos, tweets, and posts from all the parties.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The rules are very simple:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ol&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;span&gt;Pick a place to go where a bunch of people can be merry &amp;#8212; a park, a bar, a backyard, whatever&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Spread the word to local meetups, tech groups, press, etc and get people to say they&amp;#8217;ll come to your party&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;If 50 or more people RSVP to your party, we&amp;#8217;ll try to send you some WordPress stickers and buttons&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Have party attendees post photos, videos, and the like with the #wp10 hashtag&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ol&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We&amp;#8217;ll be using Meetup Everywhere to coordinate parties all over the world, so get your city on the map and &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.meetup.com/WordPress/&quot;&gt;register your party now&lt;/a&gt; !&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We&amp;#8217;ll follow up with registered organizers  over the next few weeks with some tips for how to publicize your party and to get addresses for swag packages. To that end, make sure you check the option that lets WordPress 10th Anniversary know your email, or we won&amp;#8217;t be able to get in touch with you for these things or to give you access to the WP10 blog.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Whose party will be the biggest? The most fun? The most inventive? Will it be yours?&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Note: If you already run a group on meetup.com, making your party an event in your group is great, but you still need to post it and have people RSVP at the &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.meetup.com/WordPress/&quot;&gt;special party page&lt;/a&gt;, because regular groups and Meetup Everywhere groups aren&amp;#8217;t connected yet. &lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 11 Apr 2013 13:48:42 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:8:&quot;Jen Mylo&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:37;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:87:&quot;WP Windows Phone 7: Push Notifications and a Rich Text Editor: Version 2.1 Is Available&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:42:&quot;http://wpwindowsphone.wordpress.com/?p=429&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:59:&quot;http://wpwindowsphone.wordpress.com/2013/04/11/version-2-1/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3905:&quot;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wpwindowsphone.files.wordpress.com/2013/04/wpwindowsphone-2-0-comment-push-notifications-and-rich-text-editor.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;alignright size-large wp-image-453&quot; alt=&quot;Screenshot of Version 2.1 of WordPress for Windows Phone: Rich Text Editor and Comment Push Notifications&quot; src=&quot;http://wpwindowsphone.files.wordpress.com/2013/04/wpwindowsphone-2-0-comment-push-notifications-and-rich-text-editor.png?w=300&amp;h=560&quot; width=&quot;300&quot; height=&quot;560&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;It’s that time again. Version 2.1 of WordPress for Windows Phone is out and adds some exciting new features.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We’re happy to announce that you can now get comment push notifications on your Windows Phone (OS 7.5+) which enables you to moderate comments from wherever you happen to be at the time. With 2.1 you also get a rich text editor, making it much easier to write longer posts having to deal with any HTML code.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Read on to learn what’s new or update/download version 2.1 from the Windows Phone Store right now by clicking below.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p class=&quot;download&quot;&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://windowsphone.com/s?appid=5f64ad85-f801-e011-9264-00237de2db9e&quot;&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Download App&lt;/strong&gt;WordPress for Windows Phone&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;download-info&quot;&gt;Supported: WordPress.com or self-hosted WordPress (v. 2.9+)&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Rich Text Editor&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Now you finally have the ability to use a rich text editor when creating or editing a post or page. The new editor has easy to access styling options beneath the keyboard and in the app menu, these include bulleted/numbered lists, bold, underline, and italic text. You&amp;#8217;ll also find a handy link helper among the text editing tools.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Comment Push Notifications&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you have a WordPress.com blog (or a self-hosted blog with the &lt;a href=&quot;http://jetpack.me/&quot;&gt;Jetpack plugin&lt;/a&gt;) added to the app, you can now opt in to receive push notifications for new comments. This makes it easier than ever to keep up with your readers and moderate comments while on the go. You&amp;#8217;ll get push notifications for new comments only and viewing a notification takes you right to the comment within the app. From there you can easily respond and moderate like usual.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Stability Improvements&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;In addition to the new features, we’ve worked hard on making the app even more stable. In total, almost &lt;a href=&quot;http://windowsphone.trac.wordpress.org/query?status=closed&amp;group=resolution&amp;milestone=Push+Notifications+and+Content+Editor&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;40 bugs and crashes&lt;/a&gt; have been fixed in this release.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Screenshots&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;a href=&quot;http://wpwindowsphone.wordpress.com/2013/04/11/version-2-1/#gallery-429-1-slideshow&quot;&gt;Click to view slideshow.&lt;/a&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Contributors&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The following contributors have worked on this release of WordPress for Windows Phone:  &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/support/profile/aerych&quot;&gt;aerych&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/support/profile/isaackeyet&quot;&gt;isaackeyet&lt;/a&gt;, and &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/support/profile/daniloercoli&quot;&gt;daniloercoli&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Get Involved!&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We now have a feature-driven release cycle, meaning that updates will come faster and focus on single features and enhancements. This is the perfect time to get involved in the WordPress for Windows Phone project. Check out &lt;a href=&quot;http://make.wordpress.org/mobile&quot;&gt;make.wordpress.org/mobile&lt;/a&gt; and the &lt;a href=&quot;http://windowsphonedev.wordpress.org/&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;WordPress for Windows Phone dev blog&lt;/a&gt; to see how you can get involved!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you’d like to help us translate the app into your native language, check out the &lt;a href=&quot;http://translate.wordpress.org/projects/wordpress-for-windows-phone/development&quot; target=&quot;_blank&quot;&gt;translation project&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;

&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:44:&quot;BuddyPress: BuddyPress 1.7 is now available!&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;http://buddypress.org/?p=160310&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:62:&quot;http://buddypress.org/2013/04/buddypress-1-7-is-now-available/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:8955:&quot;&lt;p&gt;BuddyPress 1.7 &amp;#8220;Totonno&amp;#8221; has arrived, and it&amp;#8217;s our best version yet!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;What&amp;#8217;s New in 1.7&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;BuddyPress 1.7 is a major feature release, containing hundreds of bugfixes and dozens of new features. We&amp;#8217;ll show off a few of our favorites below. Want to see a full changelog for 1.7? Check it out &lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.buddypress.org/developer/releases/version-1-7/&quot;&gt;on the Codex&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Theme Compatibility&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;BuddyPress&amp;#8217;s social features add new kinds of content to your WordPress site: groups, profiles, and so on. Until now, displaying that content has required building or finding a BP-compatible theme &amp;#8211; one of the biggest hurdles to using BuddyPress. Version 1.7 makes this a thing of the past. Using a feature we call &amp;#8220;theme compatibility&amp;#8221;, BuddyPress can display its content within the context of any WordPress theme &amp;#8211; no modifications required. Here are a few screenshots showing BP running on a few popular themes:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;div id=&quot;attachment_160342&quot; class=&quot;wp-caption alignleft&quot;&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://buddypress.org/wp-content/uploads/1/2013/04/bp-twentytwelve.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://buddypress.org/wp-content/uploads/1/2013/04/bp-twentytwelve-150x150.png&quot; alt=&quot;Twenty Twelve&quot; width=&quot;150&quot; height=&quot;150&quot; class=&quot;size-thumbnail wp-image-160342&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;wp-caption-text&quot;&gt;Twenty Twelve&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div id=&quot;attachment_160343&quot; class=&quot;wp-caption alignleft&quot;&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://buddypress.org/wp-content/uploads/1/2013/04/bp-coraline.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://buddypress.org/wp-content/uploads/1/2013/04/bp-coraline-150x150.png&quot; alt=&quot;Coraline&quot; width=&quot;150&quot; height=&quot;150&quot; class=&quot;size-thumbnail wp-image-160343&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;wp-caption-text&quot;&gt;Coraline&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div id=&quot;attachment_160344&quot; class=&quot;wp-caption alignleft&quot;&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://buddypress.org/wp-content/uploads/1/2013/04/bp-superstore.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://buddypress.org/wp-content/uploads/1/2013/04/bp-superstore-150x150.png&quot; alt=&quot;Woo Superstore&quot; width=&quot;150&quot; height=&quot;150&quot; class=&quot;size-thumbnail wp-image-160344&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;wp-caption-text&quot;&gt;Woo Superstore&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div&gt; &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Not satisfied with the way it looks out of the box? Not a problem. BuddyPress still provides a sophisticated, modular templating system, which you can easily customize in your own theme. Theme developers and designers can learn much more about theme compat on &lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.buddypress.org/developer/theme-development/a-quick-look-at-1-7-theme-compatibility/&quot;&gt;the BuddyPress codex&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div&gt; &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;Group Administration&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;attachment_160321&quot; class=&quot;wp-caption alignright&quot;&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://buddypress.org/wp-content/uploads/1/2013/04/dashboard.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://buddypress.org/wp-content/uploads/1/2013/04/dashboard-300x216.png&quot; alt=&quot;Group Administration in BuddyPress 1.7&quot; width=&quot;150&quot; class=&quot;size-medium wp-image-160321&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;wp-caption-text&quot;&gt;Group Administration in BP 1.7&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;If you&amp;#8217;ve run a BuddyPress-powered community site, you know that groups are a powerful way for members to connect. But there&amp;#8217;s been no way for site administrators to manage groups. BP 1.7 introduces a brand new set of Group Administration panels on your WordPress Dashboard. Now BP admins can bulk-delete groups, edit group settings, and manage group membership without ever leaving wp-admin.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div&gt; &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;em&gt;A Better Installation Experience&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;attachment_160328&quot; class=&quot;wp-caption alignright&quot;&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://buddypress.org/wp-content/uploads/1/2013/04/about.png&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=&quot;http://buddypress.org/wp-content/uploads/1/2013/04/about-150x150.png&quot; alt=&quot;About Screen&quot; width=&quot;150&quot; height=&quot;150&quot; class=&quot;size-thumbnail wp-image-160328&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;wp-caption-text&quot;&gt;About Screen&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;p&gt;BuddyPress makes it easy to add social features to your site, and BP 1.7 streamlines the process more than ever. We&amp;#8217;ve removed the installation wizard in favor of a totally automated setup &amp;#8211; just hit Activate, and we&amp;#8217;ll handle the rest. On new installations, only the Activity and Extended Profiles components are activated, helping you to start small and grow your community features bit by bit. And, following in WordPress&amp;#8217;s footsteps, we&amp;#8217;ve added About and Credits screens, helping you to get up to date on the BuddyPress project.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div&gt; &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Springtime Goodies&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;BuddyPress 1.7 is codenamed &amp;#8220;Totonno&amp;#8221;, after &lt;a href=&quot;https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Totonno%27s&quot;&gt;the legendary Brooklyn pizza joint&lt;/a&gt;. Totonno&amp;#8217;s is just a few blocks from &lt;a href=&quot;https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coney_Island_Cyclone&quot;&gt;the Cyclone&lt;/a&gt; and the Coney Island boardwalk, and there&amp;#8217;s no better end to a lovely spring day than to indulge in what may be the world&amp;#8217;s greatest pepperoni pie. With spring finally coming to Brooklyn, we think it&amp;#8217;s appropriate to honor a pizza institution with what we think will be a watershed BuddyPress release.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div&gt; &lt;/div&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;The BuddyPress Community Rocks&lt;/h3&gt;

&lt;h3&gt;Enjoy!&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Do you have questions about the latest BuddyPress release? Check out the &lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.buddypress.org&quot;&gt;BuddyPress Codex&lt;/a&gt; &amp;#8211; our growing collection of official documentation &amp;#8211; and especially the pages in &lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.buddypress.org/version/1-7/&quot;&gt;the 1.7 category&lt;/a&gt;. Volunteers are also standing by in our active &lt;a href=&quot;http://buddypress.org/support&quot;&gt;support and discussion forums&lt;/a&gt;. If you&amp;#8217;ve found a bug in BuddyPress, or if you want to contribute code to the next release, our development home is &lt;a href=&quot;http://buddypress.trac.wordpress.org&quot;&gt;buddypress.trac.wordpress.org&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;You might not be able to make it to Coney Island this summer, but we think that BuddyPress 1.7 &amp;#8220;Totonno&amp;#8221; is (almost) just as good. Download it today from the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/buddypress&quot;&gt;wordpress.org plugin repository&lt;/a&gt;, or from your WordPress Dashboard.&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Mon, 08 Apr 2013 18:51:06 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:12:&quot;Boone Gorges&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:39;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:51:&quot;WordPress.tv: Understanding the WordPress Dashboard&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:28:&quot;http://wordpress.tv/?p=18552&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:69:&quot;http://wordpress.tv/2013/04/07/understanding-the-wordpress-dashboard/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:631:&quot;&lt;div id=&quot;v-HSaaObvw-1&quot; class=&quot;video-player&quot;&gt;
&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;  &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; href=&quot;http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/gocomments/wptv.wordpress.com/18552/&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/comments/wptv.wordpress.com/18552/&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt; &lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://stats.wordpress.com/b.gif?host=wordpress.tv&amp;blog=5089392&amp;post=18552&amp;subd=wptv&amp;ref=&amp;feed=1&quot; width=&quot;1&quot; height=&quot;1&quot; /&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/2013/04/07/understanding-the-wordpress-dashboard/&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;wpdashboard.mp4&quot; src=&quot;http://videos.videopress.com/HSaaObvw/video-fba8d875a3_std.original.jpg&quot; width=&quot;160&quot; height=&quot;120&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Mon, 08 Apr 2013 06:42:33 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:12:&quot;WordPress.tv&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:40;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:63:&quot;Mark Jaquith: WordPress 3.6: shortcode_atts_{$shortcode} filter&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:40:&quot;http://markjaquith.wordpress.com/?p=3975&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:84:&quot;http://markjaquith.wordpress.com/2013/04/04/wordpress-36-shortcode-attribute-filter/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:2282:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Since WordPress 3.6 is in beta, I thought I&amp;#8217;d use this nearly-abandoned blog (hey, been busy working on WordPress!) to talk about some of the cool stuff for developers. For the first installment, check out the new &lt;code&gt;shortcode_atts_{$shortcode}&lt;/code&gt; filter. The &lt;code&gt;shortcode_atts()&lt;/code&gt; function now accepts a third parameter — the name of the shortcode — which enables the running of this filter. All of the core shortcodes now pass this parameter.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;This filter passes three things:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ol&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;code&gt;$out&lt;/code&gt; — the output array of shortcode attributes&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;code&gt;$pairs&lt;/code&gt; — the array of accepted parameters and their defaults.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;code&gt;$atts&lt;/code&gt; — the input array of shortcode attributes&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ol&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Let&amp;#8217;s look at what we can do with this. One thing is that you can dynamically set or override shortcode values. You an also define new ones, and transpose them into accepted ones. Let&amp;#8217;s look at the &amp;#8220;gallery&amp;#8221; shortcode for example. What if there was a gallery of images that you would reuse. Instead of picking the images each time, you could have a plugin that gives that set of attachment IDs a shortcut name. Then you could do &lt;code&gt;[gallery foo=my-gallery-name]&lt;/code&gt;, which the plugin would convert to a list of IDs. Or, you could enforce a certain number of gallery columns on the fly. Let someone set it theme-wide, without having them go back and change their shortcodes.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;What other uses can you think of?&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Now, if you&amp;#8217;re a plugin or theme author who provides their own shortcodes, you should immediately start providing this third parameter to your &lt;code&gt;shortcode_atts()&lt;/code&gt; calls (since it is an extra parameter, you can do this without a WordPress version check). Maybe it&amp;#8217;ll reduce the number of times people need to fork your code just to add an option to your shortcode!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;  &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; href=&quot;http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/gocomments/markjaquith.wordpress.com/3975/&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/comments/markjaquith.wordpress.com/3975/&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt; &lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://stats.wordpress.com/b.gif?host=markjaquith.wordpress.com&amp;blog=316&amp;post=3975&amp;subd=markjaquith&amp;ref=&amp;feed=1&quot; width=&quot;1&quot; height=&quot;1&quot; /&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Fri, 05 Apr 2013 03:12:05 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:12:&quot;Mark Jaquith&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:41;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:30:&quot;Dev Blog: WordPress 3.6 Beta 1&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:33:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/?p=2547&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:55:&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/2013/04/wordpress-3-6-beta-1/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4076:&quot;&lt;p&gt;WordPress 3.6 Beta 1 is now available!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;This is software still in development and &lt;strong&gt;we &lt;em&gt;really&lt;/em&gt; don’t recommend that you run it on a production site&lt;/strong&gt; — set up a test site just to play with the new version. To test WordPress 3.6, try the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/wordpress-beta-tester/&quot;&gt;WordPress Beta Tester&lt;/a&gt; plugin (you’ll want “bleeding edge nightlies”). Or you can &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/wordpress-3.6-beta1.zip&quot;&gt;download the beta here&lt;/a&gt; (zip).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We&amp;#8217;ve been working for nearly three months and have completed all the features that are slated for this release. This is a bit of a change from the betas of previous release cycles. I felt very strongly that we shouldn&amp;#8217;t release a beta if we were still working on completing the main features. This beta is &lt;strong&gt;actually a beta&lt;/strong&gt;, not an alpha that we&amp;#8217;re calling a beta. If you are a WordPress plugin or theme developer, or a WordPress hosting provider, you should absolutely start testing your code against this new version &lt;strong&gt;now&lt;/strong&gt;. More bugs will be fixed, and some of the features will get polished, but we&amp;#8217;re not going to shove in some big new feature. We&amp;#8217;re ready for you to test it, so jump in there! The more you test the beta, the more stable our release candidates and our final release will be.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;As always, if you think you’ve found a bug, you can post to the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/support/forum/alphabeta&quot;&gt;Alpha/Beta area&lt;/a&gt; in the support forums. Or, if you’re comfortable writing a reproducible bug report, &lt;a href=&quot;http://core.trac.wordpress.org/&quot;&gt;file one on the WordPress Trac&lt;/a&gt;. There, you can also find &lt;a href=&quot;http://core.trac.wordpress.org/report/5&quot;&gt;a list of known bugs&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;http://core.trac.wordpress.org/query?status=closed&amp;group=component&amp;milestone=3.6&quot;&gt;everything we&amp;#8217;ve fixed&lt;/a&gt; so far.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Here&amp;#8217;s what&amp;#8217;s new in 3.6:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Post Formats: &lt;/strong&gt; Post Formats now have their own UI, and theme authors have access to templating functions to access the structured data.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Twenty Thirteen:&lt;/strong&gt; We&amp;#8217;re shipping this year&amp;#8217;s default theme in our first release of the year. Twenty Thirteen is an opinionated, color-rich, blog-centric theme that makes full use of the new Post Formats support.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Audio/Video:&lt;/strong&gt; You can embed audio and video files into your posts without relying on a plugin or a third party media hosting service.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Autosave: &lt;/strong&gt; Posts are now autosaved locally. If your browser crashes, your computer dies, or the server goes offline as you&amp;#8217;re saving, you won&amp;#8217;t lose the your post.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Post Locking: &lt;/strong&gt; See when someone is currently editing a post, and kick them out of it if they fall asleep at the keyboard.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Nav Menus: &lt;/strong&gt; Nav menus have been simplified with an accordion-based UI, and a separate tab for  bulk-assigning menus to locations.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Revisions:&lt;/strong&gt; The all-new revisions UI features avatars, a slider that &amp;#8220;scrubs&amp;#8221; through history, and two-slider range comparisons.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Developers: &lt;/strong&gt; You make WordPress awesome(er). One of the things we strive to do with every release is be compatible with existing plugins and themes. But we need your help. &lt;strong&gt;Please test your plugins and themes against 3.6.&lt;/strong&gt; If something isn&amp;#8217;t quite right, please let us know. (Chances are, it wasn&amp;#8217;t intentional.) If you&amp;#8217;re a forward-thinking theme developer, you should be looking at implementing the new Post Format support in some of your themes (look to Twenty Thirteen for inspiration).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We&amp;#8217;re looking forward to your feedback. If you break it (i.e. find a bug), please report it, and if you’re a developer, try to help us fix it. We&amp;#8217;ve already had more than 150 contributors to version 3.6 — it&amp;#8217;s not too late to join the party!&lt;/p&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 04 Apr 2013 17:25:29 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:12:&quot;Mark Jaquith&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:42;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:35:&quot;Dougal Campbell: CodePoet Interview&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:34:&quot;http://dougal.gunters.org/?p=72513&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:77:&quot;http://dougal.gunters.org/blog/2013/04/04/dougal-campbell-codepoet-interview/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:1589:&quot;&lt;div class=&quot;featured-image align-right&quot;&gt;&lt;img width=&quot;164&quot; height=&quot;52&quot; src=&quot;http://geekramblings.gunters.netdna-cdn.com/wordpress/wp-content/uploads/2013/04/codepoet-logo.png?9bb111&quot; class=&quot;attachment-post-thumbnail wp-post-image&quot; alt=&quot;CodePoet Logo&quot; /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;!--
article.tag-codepoet div.featured-image img{background-color: #333;}
--&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I was honored to be chosen for an &lt;a title=&quot;It's me!&quot; href=&quot;http://build.codepoet.com/2013/04/04/dougal-campbell-interview/&quot;&gt;interview on CodePoet&lt;/a&gt;. Though I haven&amp;#8217;t been able to stay as involved with WordPress as much lately as I&amp;#8217;d like, due to job and family, I guess I&amp;#8217;m of &amp;#8220;historical interest&amp;#8221; because of my involvement as a core developer back in the first couple of years. (I jest &amp;#8212; a little)&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;We discuss how I came to web development and from there to WordPress, my more recent activity as a speaker at WordCamp Atlanta on the topic of security, the community and why someone should become involved, and the differences between web development as a job versus as a hobby, among other things.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I enjoyed answering the questions, and I hope you all will enjoy reading the interview!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/p&gt;
