&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Thu, 04 Apr 2013 16:03:51 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:15:&quot;Dougal Campbell&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:43;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:54:&quot;Gravatar: Gravatar and WordPress.com, Together Forever&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;http://blog.gravatar.com/?p=437&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:80:&quot;http://blog.gravatar.com/2013/04/03/gravatar-and-wordpress-com-together-forever/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:3493:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Did you know that your Gravatar.com account has always been a WordPress.com account? It&amp;#8217;s true.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Back in 2007 we (&lt;a href=&quot;http://automattic.com&quot;&gt;Automattic&lt;/a&gt;) acquired Gravatar. Heading into 2008 we &lt;a href=&quot;http://blog.gravatar.com/2008/03/14/big-changes-afoot/&quot;&gt;rewrote it in PHP&lt;/a&gt;, and ever since then, it&amp;#8217;s been using the same integrated user system as WordPress.com for accounts. Previously we handled that &amp;#8220;behind the scenes,&amp;#8221; but we found that it made things pretty confusing for everyone. We&amp;#8217;ve now switched over to using &lt;a href=&quot;http://en.support.wordpress.com/wpcc-faq/&quot;&gt;WordPress.com Connect&lt;/a&gt; exclusively, which allows you to explicitly connect Gravatar and WordPress.com, and to use your WordPress.com credentials to log into Gravatar. That&amp;#8217;s one less set of login credentials to worry about!&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;div id=&quot;attachment_438&quot; class=&quot;wp-caption aligncenter&quot;&gt;&lt;img class=&quot;size-full wp-image-438&quot; alt=&quot;wpcc-button&quot; src=&quot;http://gravatar.files.wordpress.com/2013/04/wpcc-button.png?w=258&amp;h=65&quot; width=&quot;258&quot; height=&quot;65&quot; /&gt;&lt;p class=&quot;wp-caption-text&quot;&gt;This is not a real button &lt;img src=&quot;http://s0.wp.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_smile.gif&quot; alt=&quot;:)&quot; class=&quot;wp-smiley&quot; /&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;
&lt;ol&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;span&gt;If you had a Gravatar account before, it&amp;#8217;s actually always been a WordPress.com account!&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;When you try to log in at Gravatar.com now, you will be asked to do so using WordPress.com Connect.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Once you&amp;#8217;re logged into WordPress.com, you then grant Gravatar access to use your WordPress.com account.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;After that, you&amp;#8217;ll use your WordPress.com username and password to log in to Gravatar, for evermore.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ol&gt;
&lt;p&gt;You might be wondering about existing accounts and creating new accounts, and what your options are:&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;&lt;span&gt;If you have a Gravatar account, it&amp;#8217;s actually also a WordPress.com account. You can use those details to log into WordPress.com, then grant access to Gravatar.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;If you already have a WordPress.com account, then you can use that to log into Gravatar.com now.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;li&gt;If you don&amp;#8217;t have a WordPress.com (or Gravatar) account, you can create one for free (no need for a blog, although you can do that also if you like!) and then you can grant access to Gravatar to get started.&lt;/li&gt;
&lt;/ul&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The beauty of switching to WordPress.com Connect is that it means your account information is all managed in one, super-secure place (WordPress.com), and it avoids all sorts of complexity and potential for problems with password resets, account activations, and more. We&amp;#8217;re in the process of switching all of our services to using WordPress.com Connect, so you can use the same account to log into our other nifty products, including &lt;a href=&quot;http://vaultpress.com&quot;&gt;VaultPress&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://akismet.com&quot;&gt;Akismet&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=&quot;http://polldaddy.com&quot;&gt;Polldaddy&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;There&amp;#8217;s a bunch more info on the &lt;a href=&quot;http://en.support.wordpress.com/wpcc-faq/&quot;&gt;WordPress.com Connect FAQ&lt;/a&gt;, which will hopefully help clear up any other questions you have.&lt;/p&gt;

&lt;br /&gt;  &lt;a rel=&quot;nofollow&quot; href=&quot;http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/gocomments/wptv.wordpress.com/18452/&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://feeds.wordpress.com/1.0/comments/wptv.wordpress.com/18452/&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt; &lt;img alt=&quot;&quot; border=&quot;0&quot; src=&quot;http://stats.wordpress.com/b.gif?host=wordpress.tv&amp;blog=5089392&amp;post=18452&amp;subd=wptv&amp;ref=&amp;feed=1&quot; width=&quot;1&quot; height=&quot;1&quot; /&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.tv/2013/03/28/phil-erb-wordpress-is-installed-now-what/&quot;&gt;&lt;img alt=&quot;Phil Erb: WordPress is Installed&amp;#8230; Now What?&quot; src=&quot;http://videos.videopress.com/f6li6sy6/video-50494d19a5_scruberthumbnail_0.jpg&quot; width=&quot;160&quot; height=&quot;120&quot; /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:7:&quot;pubDate&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:31:&quot;Mon, 01 Apr 2013 04:30:06 +0000&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}s:32:&quot;http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/&quot;;a:1:{s:7:&quot;creator&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:12:&quot;WordPress.tv&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}}}}i:47;a:6:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:13:&quot;
	
	
	
	
	
	
&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:100:&quot;Weblog Tools Collection: I am taking my leave of Weblog Tools Collection, and thanks for everything!&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:41:&quot;http://weblogtoolscollection.com/?p=12845&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:73:&quot;http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/weblogtoolscollection/UXMP/~3/NRKA8GMV-fA/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:4720:&quot;&lt;p&gt;Not many of the present readers might know me very well, and that in part, is the reason that I have made the decision to transfer WLTC to more willing and presently capable hands. I am a stranger on my blog and the time has come for me to make sure that this blog, its contents and its knowledge are archived and preserved and maybe rejuvenated at a later time.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;I delved into blogging tools back in 2004 when I started my Masters degree in CS. I wanted some code to mess around with in my free time and everyone was talking about blogging. I looked into a variety of tools, built a small Linux server for myself at home, and installed a few of the tools that were freely available at that time. I had a heck of a time getting a hold of MT (Moveable Type, the most well-known name) and then found b2 by sheer luck. I loved the cool look of Michael&amp;#8217;s blog and the people involved in the tool seemed to be open to comments and replied warmly to my emails and questions. Through the b2 forums I heard about WordPress and proceeded to install it on my own. To my astonishment, it worked without a hitch and I was blogging away in no time. I started looking through the code to understand how it worked and it drew me in every step of the way.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Within a few months of installing WordPress, I started to take part in the forums and wrote a few plugins and created some &amp;#8220;hacks&amp;#8221; for the tool. I even gained some notoriety with my MT VS WP post and that&amp;#8217;s when the WordPress ecosphere started to look very attractive to me. I did not do this to seek attention, but I was getting a lot of attention and I was loving it. I believe that was when Matt first noticed me and we exchanged some emails and chatted with each other. With every month and with every release of WordPress I was getting more involved. At some point I realized that I could not do it alone and hired a few interested people to help me write posts and the blog started to get popular. I brought on some advertisers to help me offset costs. Matt gave me and my blog the highest honor of being included in the WordPress Planet and that&amp;#8217;s when things really started to happen for this blog. I also started a WordPress Job blog (http://jobs.wordpress.net) which I still curate and I got involved in WordPress evangelism. Somewhere within this time, Matt had asked me to work for him at the new company he was starting and I had to turn him down because of visa restrictions and because I wanted to finish school (I kick myself every time I think about that).&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;WordPress started to mature and WordCamps started to happen. I graduated from school with a Master&amp;#8217;s Degree in Computer Science and found a job. I wanted to stay involved but it was getting bigger than I could handle. I could either dive in and get into WordPress and the blogging world, or I could focus on my job, career and family. I decided to choose the latter. I still wanted to loosely be involved with WordPress and things went well for a couple of years with me being casually involved. I even visited and spoke at a couple of WordCamps.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;When my son Lucien was born, all my time and attention was exhausted on him. I could not spend any time with WordPress or blogging at all. In addition to my growing family, I was diagnosed with a serious health condition just as I was starting a new job and moving to a new city. Needless to say, the blog was the last thing on my mind. James, who has been the sole author and curator for a long time, was my winning hand and just a fantastic helper and well wisher. He has kept things running for a long time and I have had no complaints.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;But I have found very little time to come back and spend with my old friends, Weblog Tools Collection and WordPress. I do not want this blog&amp;#8217;s content and conversations to be lost or forgotten because of my neglect. I am hoping this move will help it live on as an archive, or find new lifeblood in another form. I know that it is in the right hands.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;So Adios and Gracias. I hope to see you in another blog, and take part in another conversation with you someday. It has been a wonderful journey and I appreciate everything that has taken place because of WordPress and every bit of help and encouragement that has been provided to me by so many of you. So thank to my wonderful audience of many years, thanks to my advertisers, thanks to my authors and finally thanks to Matt and to WordPress for making my life so much more fulfilling and successful.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Peace on Earth, Goodwill to All, And to All a Goodnight!&lt;/p&gt;

&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:53:&quot;Weblog Tools Collection: Where to Find WordPress News&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:41:&quot;http://weblogtoolscollection.com/?p=12846&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:73:&quot;http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/weblogtoolscollection/UXMP/~3/ah3QRPNnlhs/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:2837:&quot;&lt;p&gt;The landscape of news has changed so much over the last few years that news about a particular topic or platform is readily available to anyone within an instant. With &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org&quot;&gt;WordPress&lt;/a&gt;, I imagine that could be one of the perks of &lt;a href=&quot;http://weblogtoolscollection.com/archives/2012/08/08/the-state-of-the-word-in-2012/&quot;&gt;powering over 16% of the web&lt;/a&gt;, but it&amp;#8217;s true that news is becoming incredibly accessible. In short, news is everywhere.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Speaking of WordPress in general, you can of course acquire official direct news from &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/news/&quot;&gt;WordPress News&lt;/a&gt;, but you can also take a peak behind the curtain and follow news in the making at &lt;a href=&quot;http://make.wordpress.org&quot;&gt;Make WordPress.org&lt;/a&gt;. Though it&amp;#8217;s only specific to the &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.com&quot;&gt;WordPress.com&lt;/a&gt; blogging platform, &lt;a href=&quot;http://en.blog.wordpress.com&quot;&gt;WordPress.com News&lt;/a&gt; is also worth watching for WordPress development news, as WordPress.com users often get access to new WordPress features before they&amp;#8217;re released, so you&amp;#8217;ll be able to try new features rather than just read about them.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;There&amp;#8217;s more news than just direct official news, like I said earlier, it&amp;#8217;s everywhere. You could subscribe to every general news site, every core developer&amp;#8217;s personal blog, every premium theme shop, and every plugin developer, but why not subscribe to a few curated news sources instead? I guess you could call &lt;a href=&quot;http://planet.wordpress.org&quot;&gt;WordPress Planet&lt;/a&gt; the official curated news source, but it&amp;#8217;s really just a collection of all news items from a particular set of curated blogs. For specific news items curated from sources through the entire WordPress community, subscribe to &lt;a href=&quot;http://poststat.us&quot;&gt;Post Status&lt;/a&gt;, and don&amp;#8217;t neglect the power of allowing the folks you follow on &lt;a href=&quot;http://twitter.com&quot;&gt;Twitter&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=&quot;http://plus.google.com&quot;&gt;Google+&lt;/a&gt;, and/or &lt;a href=&quot;http://www.facebook.com&quot;&gt;Facebook&lt;/a&gt; to curate news for you.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;Speaking of the WordPress community, you should &lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/Contributing_to_WordPress&quot;&gt;get involved&lt;/a&gt; if you aren&amp;#8217;t already. If you don&amp;#8217;t even use WordPress yet, it&amp;#8217;s time to get started &lt;a href=&quot;http://codex.wordpress.org/Getting_Started_with_WordPress&quot;&gt;with either WordPress.org&lt;/a&gt; or &lt;a href=&quot;http://learn.wordpress.com/get-started/&quot;&gt;with WordPress.com&lt;/a&gt;, share your thoughts with the world, and maybe spread some WordPress news on your blog too.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;The news is out there, and it&amp;#8217;s well within your reach. If you can&amp;#8217;t find the news, it&amp;#8217;s time to make your own.&lt;/p&gt;

&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:5:&quot;child&quot;;a:2:{s:0:&quot;&quot;;a:5:{s:5:&quot;title&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:59:&quot;Weblog Tools Collection: WordPress Plugin Releases for 3/30&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;guid&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:41:&quot;http://weblogtoolscollection.com/?p=12837&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:4:&quot;link&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:73:&quot;http://feedproxy.google.com/~r/weblogtoolscollection/UXMP/~3/-vmyakR-BnA/&quot;;s:7:&quot;attribs&quot;;a:0:{}s:8:&quot;xml_base&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;s:17:&quot;xml_base_explicit&quot;;b:0;s:8:&quot;xml_lang&quot;;s:0:&quot;&quot;;}}s:11:&quot;description&quot;;a:1:{i:0;a:5:{s:4:&quot;data&quot;;s:1089:&quot;&lt;h3&gt;New plugins&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/gc-message-box/&quot;&gt;&lt;strong&gt;GC Message Box&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/a&gt; allows you to highlight your key message(s) in smart ways within articles and blog posts.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.org/extend/plugins/simple-social-icons/&quot;&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Simple Social Icons&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/a&gt; allows you to insert social icons in any widget area.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://askwebexpert.com/stick-it/&quot;&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Stick It&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/a&gt; allows you to stick the navigation menu in any theme to the top of browser window.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;h3&gt;Updated plugins&lt;/h3&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://jetpack.me/&quot;&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Jetpack&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/a&gt; allows you to supercharge your WordPress site with powerful features previously only available to &lt;a href=&quot;http://wordpress.com/&quot;&gt;WordPress.com&lt;/a&gt; users.&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;http://blog.milandinic.com/wordpress/plugins/nav-menu-images/&quot;&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Nav Menu Images&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/a&gt; enables uploading of images for nav menu items on the menu edit screen.&lt;/p&gt;

|4|1|2013-04-25 19:28:36|2013-04-25 19:28:36|This is an example page. It's different from a blog post because it will stay in one place and will show up in your site navigation (in most themes). Most people start with an About page that introduces them to potential site visitors. It might say something like this:

&lt;blockquote&gt;Hi there! I'm a bike messenger by day, aspiring actor by night, and this is my blog. I live in Los Angeles, have a great dog named Jack, and I like pi&amp;#241;a coladas. (And gettin' caught in the rain.)&lt;/blockquote&gt;

...or something like this:

&lt;blockquote&gt;The XYZ Doohickey Company was founded in 1971, and has been providing quality doohickeys to the public ever since. Located in Gotham City, XYZ employs over 2,000 people and does all kinds of awesome things for the Gotham community.&lt;/blockquote&gt;

As a new WordPress user, you should go to &lt;a href=&quot;http://localhost:81/ZynesWordPress/wp-admin/&quot;&gt;your dashboard&lt;/a&gt; to delete this page and create new pages for your content.
